Purpose 
The purpose of this document is to standardize the lift assistants for assembly production 
lines, from their planning, implementation, and maintenance stage. 
 
Introduction 
Lift assistants are all those devices that help the operator to load and transport from point 
A to point B in a delimited area; pieces that exceed 14 kg/32 lbs such as rails and/or some 
crossmembers. They vary depending on their function and use. Metalsa refers to these 
devices as lift assistants  
 
There is another loading assistant called a spring balancer, which helps to have tools at 
hand and move them without any problem in a certain area, this is useful when the tool 
cable is not obstructing the operation and/or there are space restrictions. 
 
Objective 
This Standard seeks to provide the proper lift assistant in workstations to ensure the 
correct performance of each worker's duties and to maintain a safe and healthy 
environment. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
 
1. Lift Assistants 
The Lift assistants are required when the process implicates a team member to manipulate 
parts or containers with a high frequency such as 1 or 2 parts per minute during an 8 hrs. 
shift with a weight greater than 32 lbs. or 14 kg., in order to ensure the team member 
does not suffer any injury. 
 
To determine when a lift assistant should be used, the following calculations are made: 
 
Calculation: 
 
Lift assistants are classified by the workstations on which they are used: 
• Sub-Assemblies 
• Stacking Stations (Main Line) 
• Inspect and repair stations 
 
 
 
 
 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
2. Stacking Stations (Main Line) 
 
2.1 Crane 
A crane is a machinery that lifts, lowers, and 
moves heavy or bulky loads. They are 
equipped with components that provide 
mobility in 3 axes (x, y, and z). 
 
 
 
 
2.1.1 Operational Requirements for Crane (Beams system) 
1. For the Lift Assist in the Main Line 
unloading area, there must be a catwalk 
with 
stairs 
to 
allow 
for 
easy 
maintenance/replacement of the hoist. 
 
2. It must be prepared for a backup system 
for quick replacement in case of failure, 
especially on the mainline. 
 
3. Each 
hoist 
must 
have 
its 
own 
independent FRL. The Filtration and 
Regulation system should be at floor level for easy access for maintenance team, while 
the Lubrication system should be at the same height or higher than the hoist so that 
the lubrication work is not affected. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Illustrative image taken from the DS line in Apodaca. 
Illustrative Image 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
2.1.2 Safety Requirements for Crane (Beams system) 
1. Must consider two "runaway beam hard stops" 
at the end of the section or range of the 
equipment being installed, also trolls must 
have locking nuts or a key. 
2. Have security steel cable to the trolley and rail 
according to the weight of the equipment 
being loaded. 
3. Get a report of structural design in order to 
ensure 
the 
correct 
evaluation 
due 
to 
vibrations in the structure. 
4. All access to the conveyor (upstairs) must have 
an interlock mechanism in order to eliminate 
the risk with moving equipment. 
5. All overhead bolts need to be safety wired 
6. The crane integrator/supplier has to deliver all 
relevant documentation of the structure to 
Metalsa for its release (signed design among others). 
7. A safety analysis/assessment must be performed regarding the safe operation of crane 
loading/unloading by a third party.  
 
 
 
Reference images taken from the DT stacking crane. 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
3. Sub-Assemblies 
3.1 Ergo Arm / Articulating Arms 
Help to reduce operator fatigue by absorbing torque reaction and allowing for effortless 
lifting and manipulating of products.  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
3.1.1 Suppliers 
These are the recommended supplier 
options to quote hoists. For more options, 
please refer to the following document: 
Equipment Standard List 
• Indeva 
• Knight Industries 
NOTE: The use of retractable Ergo Arms is forbidden 
 
 
 
Illustrative image taken from the DS line in Apodaca. 
Illustrative image taken from the JL line in Apodaca. 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
3.1.2 Operational Requirements for ergo arms 
1. The movement it performs must reach at least 500 mm/sec. 
2. It must have a minimum radius of 3 mts. Any other range must be consulted and 
approved by Metalsa. 
3. The ergo arm must have a load capacity of 1/2 ton to 1 ton. This must be rectified and 
confirmed according to the product to be handled and all other components to be 
equipped (hoist, hoses, steel wire ropes, etc.). 
4. They must be pneumatic Equipment. 
 
3.1.3 Safety Requirements for ergo arms 
1. As a "moving" object, it must 
be painted orange. 
2. It is required that the base of 
the structure be fastened 
with chemical anchors. 
3. The 
minimum 
diameter 
allowed of the flange/anchor 
must be a minimum of ¾” (in 
case the calculation obtained 
demands more). 
4. The integrator must provide a structural design report to ensure proper assessment 
due to vibrations in the structure. 
5. It must be considered a location for the FRL systems where it cannot be hit by the 
same movement of the piece or by the operator in its normal path. 
6. The FRL should avoid contact with water to prevent malfunctioning. 
7. Each Lift Assist must have its FRL unit which must be installed as close as possible to 
the application. The Filtration and Regulation system should be at floor level for easy 
access for maintenance team, while the Lubrication system should be at the same 
height or higher than the hoist so that the lubrication work is not affected 
8. The load capacity must be specified in TON or Lb in USA, and TON or Kg in México. 
9. The structure must have a safety factor of 5 according to ASME B30.
 
Illustrative image taken from the DT line in Apodaca. 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
10. The structure must have a guarantee point for the tightening of all bolts. 
 
11. The safety cables must have at least 2 wire rope clamps and their nuts have a warranty 
point.  
 
 
 
12. The rails that support the trolley and hoist must have a double physical stop. 
 
 
3.2 Trolley 
The trolley is the mechanism that moves the hoist along the 
bridge girder of a crane. The hoist is moved horizontally along 
the top or underside of the bridge girder to position it above 
a load. 
The following requirements applies also for Stacking Stations 
 
 
3.2.1 Suppliers 
These are the recommended supplier options to 
quote hoists. For more options, please refer to 
the following document: Equipment Standard 
List 
• Ingersoll Rand 
 
Illustrative Image 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
3.2.2 Operational-Safety Requirements for Trolleys 
1. A heavy-duty 4-wheel trolley with at least 20% more than the design rated load 
capacity. 
2. Trolleys must have a safety nut and a steel cable in case it falls. 
3. It must have a security steel cable of at least 1/8” (to the trolley and rail according to 
the weight of the equipment being loaded. 
4. A support trolley should be considered for all hoists at the end or beginning of the 
track, depending on the need. 
5. It is important that cotter pin is considered for the nuts 
6. It is considered a bad practice to adjust the trolley with washers to the width of the 
tires for the rail, therefore Metalsa does not approve this practice. A custom bushing 
must be used. 
7. It is considered a bad practice to adjust the trolley with washers to the width of the 
tires for the rail, therefore Metalsa does not approve this practice. A bushing that fits 
the trolley properly must be used. 
8. The trolley must have more than 2 bolts attached to the rail to prevent it from opening 
easily due to constant movement. 
 
 
9. The trolley must have a safety cable to prevent a possible fall.  
 
 
 
3.3 Hoist motor 
Hoists are situated on the primary horizontal beam of the crane 
or ergo arm, called the bridge girder. The hoist, when connected 
to the trolley, moves back and forth across the bridge girder 
The following requirements applies also for Stacking Stations 
 
 
 
Illustrative Image 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
3.3.1 Suppliers 
These are the recommended supplier options to 
quote hoists. For more options, please refer to 
the following document: Equipment Standard 
List 
• Ingersoll Rand 
 
3.3.2 Operational Requirements for Hoists 
1. Must have two Runway Beam End Stop at the end 
of the section or range of the equipment being 
installed, also trolls must have locking nuts or a 
key. 
 
2. The hoist must be pneumatic, any other type such 
as electric is not allowed in production lines. 
 
3. The hoist must be chain type, any material other 
than chain such as steel wire rope is not allowed. 
 
4. All hoist baskets (where the chain is stored) should 
be made of PVC/Steel, as fabric baskets wear out 
quickly. 
 
 
 
5. Each Lift Assist must have its FRL unit which must be installed as close as possible to 
the application. The Filtration and Regulation system should be at floor level for easy 
access for maintenance team, while the Lubrication system should be at the same 
height or higher than the hoist so that the lubrication work is not affected 
 
6. A pump must be considered at the bottom of the ergo arm to refill the oil (lubrication 
system). 
 
7. All hoist applications must have a spiral hose (air intake). 
 
The chain container is made of PVC or Steel. 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
8. The air hose has to be according to the length of the arm (not too long so that it hangs 
down) In addition, this hose should have a steel cable as a guide, so that the hose does 
not hang down. 
 
9. It must have a load capacity of 500 kg to 1 ton. It must be confirmed/assured that it is 
in accordance with the product to be handled (A capacity of 1/4 ton for rails and 1/2 
ton for modules/splices is recommended) The selection of any hoist with a capacity 
greater than that indicated must be consulted and approved by Metalsa. 
 
10. The hoist control must have a guard to protect them from impact.  
 
4. It is recommended to have 2 hoists in the area where they are needed, so that the 
operation does not stop in case one of them fails, especially on the mainline. 
 
3.3.3 Maintenance requirements 
1. A mechanical and pneumatic kit must be kept in storage for maintenance work on the 
hoist. This maintenance must be carried out every 6 months. 
 
2. It is important that spare parts for the brake and transmission of the hoist, as well as 
hoses and spare parts for the hoist control as well, must always be available in 
warehouse. 
 
3. A catwalk or movable ladder should be provided to allow the maintenance team to 
remove the hoist for maintenance work. 
 
 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
Illustrative image of hoist load capacity indicator 
3.3.4 Safety requirements for Hoists 
1. A 1/2 inch steel cable must always be used to 
support the chain from the hoist (the steel 
cable must be more tensioned than the hoist 
chain so that part of the load is supported by 
the steel cable). 
 
2. Must have a 1/2" safety cable at the top of the 
hoist (Is consider as a safety device in case the 
trolley fails.). 
 
3. The hoist chain stop should be positioned 1 
meter from the hoist hook.  
 
4. In addition, the hoist control must be secured 
with a 1/8" steel cable to prevent it from 
falling  
 
5. For the installation of the equipment, the 
manufacturer's installation guidelines must be 
followed in order to maintain the safety of the operators and the correct operation of 
the equipment. 
 
6. The lifting capacity of the hoist must be displayed in a visible place.  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
7. The hoist must have safety latches on its hooks.  
 
The guide cable for the air hose and the guard for the 
hoist's pushbutton panel. 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
8. The hoist must have a safety cable to the rail or trolley.  
 
9. The hoist must have safety stops on the chain. 
 
 
 
 
3.4 End Effector/Gripper 
End Effectors are devices that can be manually, mechanically or powered to meet the 
requirements of your application. They perform the gripping of a material and allow the 
operator to handle it safely. 
Metalsa considers hook end effectors as the best option due to their effectiveness, ease 
of use and safety. 
Hook End Effectors quickly connect and disconnect to designated areas of the product or 
fixture. Most applications tend to be straight lift and transfer with no manipulation of the 
product. 
 
This info Applies also for Stacking Stations 
Illustrative Image 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
3.4.1 Operational-Safety Requirements for End Effector 
1. Having a guard or scanner to protect the area of risk. 
2. When choosing the gripper, the type of rack/container to be used to deposit the part 
must also be considered, in order to avoid incompatibility or difficulty in the process. 
To know the types of racks/containers, consult the standard "Assembly Packaging 
Equipment". 
3.5 Safety BuyOff Required 
Must review the following Buy Off to ensure that all bullets are completed. 
 
 
 
 
4. Inspect and Repair Stations 
 
4.1 Spring Balancers 
Spring balancers help the operator increase productivity and 
provide convenience by placing frequently used tools within 
easy access to them, while at the same time helping to reduce 
damage to the tools themselves. Spring Balancers provide 
the operator with an organized and safe work area while 
helping to reduce fatigue. It gives the operator the 
opportunity to take the tool, pull it, use it and when released, 
it will return to its place of origin so that the operator can 
continue with the process without it getting in the way. 
 
4.2 Suppliers 
These are the recommended supplier options to 
quote spring balancers. For more options, please 
refer to the following document: Equipment 
Standard List 
• Ingersoll Rand 
 
 
Illustrative Image 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
4.3 Requirements for tool balancers 
1. The tool balancers should only be used for hand tools whose arrangement in the 
layout is restricted due to space constraints. 
2. The use of any tool balancers with a load capacity between 100 and 150 kg should be 
consulted with the safety team. Any tool balancer with a load capacity above 150 kg 
is prohibited for operation. 
 
 
5. FAQs  
• What is the capacity that an ergo arm should have? 
The capacity of the hoist should be approximately 1/2 ton to 1 ton. Although this figure is 
dependent on the weight of the product to be handled (rails, modules, splices, etc.) and 
various components such as the hoist itself, hoses, steel wire ropes, trolley, etc. 
 
• What is the load capacity that the hoist must have? 
The capacity of the hoist will depend on the product to be handled, as well as all the 
components to be loaded. It is recommended to be between 1/2 ton to 1 ton although this has 
to be rectified. 
 
• What type of end effector/gripper should I use for the hoist? 
Depending on the operation and the product, it varies. It should be according to the GD&T 
Specifications 
 
• What should be the reach of the ergo arm? 
Varies depending on the operation, it is recommended to be between 2 and 3 meters. 
 
• If current projects do not comply with any point of the standard, is it necessary 
to change/update it in order to comply? 
It is up to the discretion and consideration of each plant coordinator. It is 
recommended that the specifications contained in this standard be followed as it seeks 
to prevent production failures.

1. INTENT 
1.1 These standards have been written by Metalsa, for the purpose of providing guidelines for the quotation of 
the assembly process. 
1.2 It is required for the Quotation of assembly process to guarantee the safety of our workers, the quality of 
our products and the capital invested, as well as offer to our customers a flexible, innovative and integral 
competitive assembly process which put our proposals above the competition. 
1.3 It is responsibility of the VP area to ensure that they are in possession of the latest revision of this 
quotation guideline prior quoting or working on any job. Our standards will be made available to our 
suppliers by authorized personal from purchasing area. 
2. SCOPE 
2.1 This Guideline is effective for all new process quoted (Value proposition area), Current process 
engineering changes & Capacity Up adaptation (Product Management), Improvements (Process 
Engineering & Operations). 
3. RESPONSABILITIES 
3.1 Metalsa as a Global company shall comply with this Guidelines for the scope already explained above.  
3.2 This document specify the Minimum Guidelines for all processes. If a requirement do not comply with this 
document the contractor shall fill a Feasible Change Request (FCR) an wait for Metalsa´s approval 
following the FCR flow. 
3.3 If any location finds any better practice than the ones present here department shall notify to Knowledge 
Center KC in order to determine if the guide shall suffer any modification. 
3.4 Because the regulation on each country are different every area is responsible to comply with the Federal 
and local Laws on each process at your location. 
3.5 HARDCOPIES OF THIS FILE ARE UNCONTROLLED. Controlled Documents reside electronically on the 
MOS portal. 
3.6 For link to controlled document contact Automation Operations Advance Manufacturing (OAM). 
3.7 Individuals using an uncontrolled copy are responsible for ensuring that they are using the latest revision of 
this document.

1. GENERAL 
1.1 Contractor Responsibilities. 
1.2 Contractors shall participate in a pre-job safety review to discuss safety, health, and environmental policies 
and procedures that shall be followed while performing work on Metalsa's premises. The contractor 
management representative who will be on-site will be required to participate in this meeting.  Contractors 
are responsible for supplying all the safety equipment request for their employees. 
1.2.1 Before ordering any material or starting any work, the contractor shall verify all measurements at the 
site and/or building and be responsible for the correctness of same.  Extra compensation cannot be 
allowed for differences between actual measurements and those indicated on drawings. Any 
discrepancies found shall be submitted for correction and approval before work proceeds. 
1.2.2 Contractors shall be responsible for correctly bounded and earth grounding of all equipment they 
install. 
1.2.3 Contractors shall be responsible for correctly electrical grounding of all equipment they install. 
1.2.4 Contractors shall be responsible to vacuum and clean panels of all debris at the end of the Final 
Buyoff. 
1.2.5 Electrical equipment shall be tested by the installer to ensure cable continuity, proper connections, 
proper grounding, correct rotation of motors, and proper controls wiring connections, this to ensure 
correct controls operation. This shall happen after installation at Metalsa Plant has been completed. 
1.2.6 Contractor is responsible for debugging all the controls and wiring.  
1.2.7 Contractor is responsible to make the temperature and humidity calculation of the devices in order to 
estimate if a cooling system is required. 
1.2.8 Metalsa supplied equipment shall not be modified in a way that would void the warranty of the 
equipment from the supplier. 
1.2.9 Integrator shall not modify any device or component that would void any warranty. 
1.2.10 All equipment software and firmware version shall not be obsolete. 
1.2.11 All equipment used shall not be at the end of the device life cycle. 
1.3 Designs and Workmanship 
1.3.1 Shall be in accordance with the requirements of the contract documents and subject to acceptance 
by Metalsa. 
1.3.2 Every device must have a part number and at least one year in the market 
1.3.3 Components shall be by the latest type/model and design manufactured for the intended use and 
shall be laid out and installed such as to afford easy maintenance and/or replacement without major 
disassembly of adjacent parts.  
1.3.4 The supplier shall submit bills of material and/or catalog cuts approved by Metalsa prior to component 
purchase or fabrication. 
1.3.5 Any commercial or third-party equipment used by supplier, which does not meet Metalsa’s 
specifications and was not approved, shall be replaced by supplier. The supplier will be 100% 
responsible for the costs of such equipment replacements.  
1.3.6 The supplier shall be responsible for the set-up and calibration of all the components and equipment. 
1.3.7 Metalsa encourages suggestions for technological advancements. Supplier will supply justification for 
the new technology.  
1.4 Inspections 
1.4.1 Authorized representatives of Metalsa shall have access to the supplier’s plant, at any reasonable 
time, to inspect equipment, sub-assemblies or parts, and to obtain information on work progress and 
delivery. 
1.5 Codes and Regulations 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page10 
1.5.1 Provide electrical equipment to meet the applicable requirements for the Region / Country of the 
equipment final location. 
1.5.2 Reference guidelines:                               
1.5.2.1 Metalsa’s Specification 
1.5.2.2 Latest Standards of IEEE 
1.5.2.3 NEMA 
1.5.2.4 JIC 
1.5.2.5 The National Electric Code (NEC) (latest issue) 
1.5.2.6 Department of Labor – Occupational Safety and Health Administration (OSHA) (ANSI) 
1.5.2.7 NFPA (latest issue) 
1.5.2.8 EC Directives (European Community) 
1.5.2.9 ANSI/RIA R15.06 (Latest Release) 
1.5.2.10 IEC (International Electrotechnical Commission) 
1.5.2.11 IEC 61439-1 and -2 
1.5.2.12 International Standards (ISO) 
1.5.3 If differences between specifications, codes and standards occur, the highest requirements shall 
apply.  
1.5.4 If there is any Inspection and certification required. It shall be the responsibility of the supplier. 
1.5.5 Where the supplier is furnishing control panels and control components as an integral part of a 
machine or group of machines, the control shall meet all of Metalsa’s standards, codes and safety 
requirements (“Metalsa Safety Requirement Global Standard”). 
1.5.6 There shall be a revision of the designs, and Metalsa has to approve those designs in order for the 
supplier to purchase the items. The supplier may apply for a variance from Metalsa's specifications. All 
variances shall include any pertinent technical data, catalog numbers, manufacturer and, when apply; 
shop drawings. These variances shall be accepted on the revision and approval of the designs. If a 
variance from Metalsa’s specifications is made without Metalsa consent, by any additional cost the 
supplier shall replace that item or items for the ones that Metalsa specify. 
1.5.7 The supplier shall be responsible for acceptance of installation and connection to panel(s) by the 
variety of crafts involved in the field, unless Metalsa waives this requirement. 
1.5.8 Metalsa’s representative before shipment shall validate all panels (Buyoff). 
1.6 For safety measures/requirements please refer to Metalsa Standard “Safety Global Requirements”.  
2. CONTROL PANELS AND ENCLOSURES 
2.1 Enclosures Voltage 
2.1.1 Only 24VCD is permitted inside Remote IO Enclosure, alternated voltage current (VAC) isn’t allowed. 
(Any specific actuator that needs VAC should be reviewed and approved by Metalsa). 
2.1.2 Only Main System enclosure and Zone Enclosure can have VAC and shall be insulated from other 
components. 
2.1.3 High voltage shall be separated or segregated from low voltage.  
2.2 Enclosures 
2.2.1 Enclosures inside the building shall be NEMA12 or IP54. 
2.2.2 Enclosures inside the building workcells or exposed to dust shall be NEMA4 or IP65. 
2.2.3 All enclosures exposed to liquids shall be at least NEMA6 or IP67 
2.2.4 Devices on machine shall be at least IP67 
2.2.5 Devices inside of cabinet shall be at least IP20 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page11 
2.2.6 Colors shall be Metalsa specified. 
2.2.7 Stainless steel panels and fiberglass panels, if required, shall not be painted.  
2.2.8 Enclousre installation shall meet OSHA or Local Standard.  
2.2.9 Enclosures shall be installed on safety fence unless a floor mounting is required, Metalsa written 
consent is required prior mounting design. 
2.2.10 Unless otherwise noted on the drawings, a twelve-inch floor stand shall be supplied where floor 
mounting is required, if the specified mounting enclosure is not designed for direct floor mounting. 
2.2.11 The stand shall be constructed of identical material, and finish as the enclosure to suit the 
environmental requirements. (tooling manual section 22.2.1” Inputs-outputs (I-O)). 
2.2.12 Construction of stand shall permit unobstructed access to the floor for cleaning purposes.  
2.2.13 All j-boxes shall use DIN RAIL standoffs for the terminals. Terminals are not allowed to be mounted 
to a back plate directly.                     
2.2.14 Components mounted within an enclosure shall not interfere with the removal of any other 
component. 
2.2.15 All the panels shall have enough space to open completely the doors.  
2.2.16 All enclosures housing a PLC shall have a laptop shelf within standard patchcable distance (3 Feet), 
110vac outlet and Ethernet network access port, accessible without opening enclosure door. 
2.2.17 Manufacturer's identification, panel and device nameplates shall be easily visible identifying their 
number, function, I/O address and network address (if required).   
2.2.17.1 All operator devices, solenoids, motor starter, etc. shall have permanently attached by white 
lamicoid nameplates with black letters  
2.2.17.2 In safety devices shall have a Red lamicoid nameplates with white letters.   
2.2.17.3 In cabinets were the power disconnect does not remove all the energy, a yellow lamicoid with 
black letters shall be used stating the Caution 
 
2.2.17.4 In areas exposed directly to welding, burning, or high temperature; nameplates shall be 
engraved in aluminum or stainless steel tags, in order to avoid for the lamicoid to burn and no 
longer be functional, the decision to put the aluminum or stainless steel tags, shall be decided 
during design.  
2.2.18 All cables and connectors shall be labeled with a permanent lamicoid tag inside and outside of the 
cabinet (Reference labeling standard document for the names). 
2.2.19 Every Floor Mounted Panels shall have a system of illumination with LED Lamps (most of the cases 
the lamp is of 24Vdc) , for the illumination inside the panel. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page12 
2.2.20 All enclosures shall have an equipment nameplate stating supply voltage, full load current, in rush 
current, NFPA arc-flash rating, NFPA protective gear requirements and interrupting capacity and 
480vac bus origin mounted on the front door.  
2.2.21 Proper ferrules shall be used for all wires in enclosures. (If there is any reason to not use them, in 
design a Metalsa deviation is required). 
2.2.22 Metalsa panels layout templates shall be provided and followed. 
 
2.3 Wiring Methods 
2.3.1 Components shall not be connected directly from the main power supply to the final actuator, it shall 
have a control component.  
2.3.2 All conductors exiting the control panel shall terminate at a terminal block, bulkhead or a rectangular 
connector (Ex. Harting plug connector) 
2.3.3 Vertically mounted fuse holders shall have line connection made at the top. 
2.3.4 Horizontally mounted fuse holders shall have line connection made at the left.   
2.3.5 Where cables run through panel walls from outside the enclosure.  Watertight strain relief connectors 
style shall be used. 
 
2.3.6 For control cables tie mounting pads shall be used.  
  
2.3.7 Cables tie mounting pads shall be used every 3 inches. 
 
2.3.8 Cable cleats shall be used if high voltage supply is run thru the enclosure 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page13 
 
 
2.3.9 Arrangements 
2.3.9.1 Supplier shall arrange components to make the most economical use of panel space. 
2.3.9.2 Components shall not be mounted below starters and contactors to avoid particles from arcing 
contacts falling into other components. 
2.3.9.3 All control power wiring shall be located above PLC I/O racks and module wiring. I/O terminal 
blocks should be located below PLC.  
 
2.3.9.4 NOTE:  The image is a suggestion of the components arrangement in backplane, the supplier is 
responsible of the proposed design.  
 
2.3.10 Spacing 
2.3.10.1 Components and wire ways shall be spaced so that all wire terminations are readily 
accessible.  Space shall be adequate to remove or service any component without loosening or 
removing adjacent components. 
2.3.10.2 20% usable space shall be left for future use on enclosures, trays and wire ways unless 
waived by Metalsa. 
2.3.10.3 At least 20% usable space shall be left for future use for I/O modules, Racks slots, 
Communication switches, etc.  
 
2.3.11 Mounting 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page14 
2.3.11.1 Holes shall be drilled and tapped in back panel for mounting components. 
2.3.11.2 Items not normally required for external operation or visual observation (for example HMI, 
Push Buttons, Lamps) shall be mounted on back panels only. 
2.3.11.3 It is not permitted to mount components on the back of the panel, they shall be mounted on a 
mounting panel. 
2.3.11.4 All devices shall be mounted in a position recommended by the device manufacturer for long 
life and for best performance of the device. 
2.3.11.5 No device shall be mounted in a position where moving parts of the device may hang up due 
to abnormal friction. (Ex. Main disconnector hanging up with a cable) 
2.3.11.6 Wiring shall not be mounted close to any moving part in a moving fixture if they may hang up. 
(Ex. Movil bolsters, AGV, Transfer units, Conveyors, etc..) 
2.3.11.7 No components or devices should be mounted on the sides, top plate or bottom plate of the 
inside of the enclosure without the written consent of Metalsa. 
2.3.11.8 Heavy components mounted on plug-in sockets shall be mounted so that normal action of 
gravity should retain the device in its plug-in socket, or shall be held in place with locking clips or a 
locking mechanism.  
 
 
 
2.3.12 Terminal Blocks 
 
2.3.12.1 Terminal blocks shall be pressure plate type (Rail Din mounted). 
2.3.12.2 Vertically mounted terminal block shall have line connections made at top. Any deviation shall 
have Metalsa Approval and in the enclosure shall clearly state the connection style used. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page15 
2.3.12.3 Horizontally mounted terminal block shall have line connections made at left. Any deviation 
shall have Metalsa Approval and in the enclosure shall clearly state the connection style used. 
2.3.12.4 Terminal block marking strips shall identify all the active terminals. 
2.3.12.5 1.5” inches (minimum) shall be provided as space between terminal blocks and wire ways. 
2.3.12.6 Spare terminals shall be provided in a 20% of active terminals. 
2.3.13 Not more than two conductors greater than 22 AWG shall be held under one terminal screw. Where 
conductor size is 22 AWG or smaller four conductors shall be allowed. Factory provided jumper may be 
used and shall not be counted as a conductor. 
2.3.14 Vertically mounted terminal block shall have line connections made at top. 
2.3.15 Horizontally mounted terminal block shall have line connections made at left. 
2.3.16 When connections to manufacturers equipment terminals are required, the connections shall be 
made using fork tongue insulated terminals or equal.  
2.3.17 In connection to bolt terminals a crimp terminal shall be used (fork tongue or ring connector), bare 
wire shall not be used. 
 
 
2.3.17.1 For visual management for the terminal block the color coding is:  
Color 
Usage 
Red 
AC Power, Control 
White 
AC Common 
Blue 
DC Power,  Control, Common 
Yellow 
Power originating in external 
panel 
Gray 
Signal/Communications 
Green / Yellow 
Grounding 
 
2.3.18 Wire ducts 
2.3.18.1 A minimum of 25% free space in trough shall be provided. 
2.3.18.2 Cables shall be secured every 3 inches. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page16 
 
2.3.18.3 All excess wire shall be trimmed back to the correct size.   
4.2  Circuit Breakers 
2.3.19 Circuit protection should be in accordance to UL standards. 
2.4  Fuses and Fuse Holders 
2.4.1 All fuse holders shall have a finger safe. 
2.4.2 All fuses and holders shall meet NFPA Arc-flash requirements. 
2.4.3 Miniature class fuses are prohibited. Unless approved by Metalsa. 
2.4.4 All fuses shall have a “blown” status indicators. 
2.4.5 Power feed shall be at the top of fuse terminal connections.Unless approved by Metalsa. 
2.4.6 Motor starter fuse holders shall be mounted directly above the motor starter. 
2.4.7 Proprietary fuses are not allowed. Unless approved by Metalsa. 
2.4.8 Control circuits using #16 wires shall not be fused at more than 10 amperes.  
2.4.9 All fuse holders and fuses supporting disconnects, starter circuits and the primary side of the control 
transformer on any 460 volts, 230 volts, or 208 volts’systems have to use 600 volts rated fuses and 
fuse holders.  Miniature style fuses and fuse blocks shall not be used for this purpose. 
2.4.10 All fuses for new or replacement purposes on 480/240-volt systems shall be current limiting type, 
UL. RK-1 or as otherwise directed.  All fusible equipment for 480/240-volt systems shall be equipped 
with rejection-type fuse holders designed to prohibit the use of non-current limiting type fuses.  Non-
current limiting fuses (UL class "K") shall not be permitted.  Renewable link type fuses are prohibited. 
It´s acceptable to use LPN (250V) and LPS (600V) or LP-CC and J. 
2.4.11 All incabinet 24-volt power supplies should have positive side of secondary fused. 
2.4.12 All PLC local/remote outputs shall be fused according to output card ratings. Using electronically 
fused output cards shall be allowed in place of standard outputs coupled with DIN rail mounted fuses in 
the event supplier can show adequate and easy method of resetting electronically tripped fuse.  
Metalsa approval required.  
2.4.12.1 Supplier can request the absence of fuses in case it´s use electronically protected I/O devices 
with no external fuse required or in the case that the signal goes as an input to another device 
inside the cabinet. This request shall require Metalsa approval.   
2.4.13 Where applies each PLC Local/Remote Input(greater than 24VDC)/Output/Analog Module shall 
have individual control voltage protection fuses or circuit braker. 
2.5  Power Distribution Blocks 
2.5.1 Always after the disconnect switch or isolation contactor (when applies) a Power Distribution blocks 
shall be used. 
2.5.2 Power distribution blocks greater than 50V shall have finger safe guard. 
2.5.3 Power distribution blocks shall be sized to match the disconnect switch rating. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page17 
 
2.6 Control Voltages and Transformer  
2.6.1 Control voltage shall be 24 VDC unless Metalsa approval. 
2.6.2 For 120 VAC control a three phase primary with 120 volts secondary Transformer shall be used. 
2.6.3 Voltages above 480vac shall be finger safe, grouped, isolated, and identified with the voltage, in 
addition to the above listed requirements. 
2.6.4 Any equipment that does not feed thru a Power distribution panel (PDP) shall have a surge 
suppressor module. 
2.6.5 In case a IP67 power supply is not used. All remote cabinets containing I/O modules and field devices 
shall have their own 24vdc power feed from the Main Panel, capable of meeting power requirements for 
that cabinet. 
2.6.6 Pneumatic solenoids, hydraulic solenoids, motor starter coils, pilot lamps, safety circuits, interlock 
signals, HMI and field devices shall be 24vdc. (Any change from this shall be approved by Metalsa). 
2.6.7 All 24-volt power supplies shall only be ground once in the cabinet that is installed (Isolated 
grounded). 
2.6.8 The input voltage for all the 24Volt power supplies shall be AC 100 - 240V, in case we need a 24Volt 
power supply with AC above 240V Input, Metalsa approval is required. 
2.6.9 24 Volt Power Supplies shall have conformal coating. 
2.6.10 The use of IP67 or in cabinet power source shall be approved by Metalsa. 
2.6.11  
2.6.12 One side of the control transformer secondary shall be grounded to a common grounding point in 
the cabinet. 
2.6.13 The ungrounded side of the secondary of the control transformer shall be fused. 
2.6.14 All transformers shall have 25% spare capacity. 
 
2.7  Disconnects 
2.7.1 Any enclosure with voltages higher than 24V or 120AC shall have a Disconnects 
2.7.2 Quick disconnect shall be used for power distribution in Robot Controlers and Welding Machines. 
 
2.7.3 Disconnects shall have LOTO option 
2.7.4 Disconnect shall be so arranged that door(s) cannot be opened unless the disconnect is in the "off" 
position.   
2.7.5 Through door disconnects shall not be allowed. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page18 
2.7.6 A normally open contact shall be provided on disconnects for devices that needs to be monitored. 
2.7.7 Foreign supply voltages above 24vcd 120vac entering a control panel is prohibited without Metalsa 
written consent.  
2.7.8 Foreign voltages entering the panel shall have a means provided to isolate them from the panel 
interior.  This may be accomplished by auxiliary contacts on the panel disconnect, an external relay, or 
internal fuses where the foreign voltage enters the panel.  A warning sign shall be provided on panels 
containing foreign voltages (yellow with black lettering). 
2.7.9 All motors shall have a non-fusible safety switch with auxiliary contact located within fifteen feet of the 
motor. Contact shall be wired back to PLC for monitoring. This specification may be waived for 
applications using servo-motors.  
2.7.10 Motor control panel is in line of sight of the motor and within ten feet of the motor the motor control 
panel disconnect will be used as the motor safety switch.  
2.8 Identification 
2.8.1 Panels / enclosures labels shall be lamicoid. 
2.8.2 Cables, Hoses / Flex Conduits should be labeled with plastic labels (Refer to next picture). Shall be 
labeled at both ends with identification according to drawings as well as point of origin and destination. 
 
2.8.3 All panel wiring shall be labeled with “wrap around” label which has transparent protective cover. 
2.8.4 For high temperature or greasy processes (ex. Hydroforming, press) use a transparent termofit over 
the “wrap around” label. 
2.8.5 Device IP Addresses shall be clearly marked on inside of panels at the device and on the outside of 
panel with Device Name. 
2.8.6 All disconnects shall have a lamicoid tag providing the motor name and the source from which the 
motor is connected to 
2.8.7 Label description shall use the specification of the file “Devices and cable nomenclature” 
 
2.9  Isolation of Electrical Components 
2.9.1 In common control panels containing electrical as well as mechanical, hydraulic (cooling systems) 
and pneumatic equipment, electrical components shall be totally separately or Isolated from oil and 
dust by tight barriers between the electrical and mechanical sections. 
2.9.2 Electrical conductors installed between the electrical section and individual components in the 
mechanical, hydraulic (cooling systems) and/or pneumatic section shall be installed in an approved 
raceway and terminated with approved fittings. 
2.9.3 If applicable all mechanical, hydraulic and pneumatic equipment requiring connections to the 
electrical system shall be grounded.

Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page19 
2.10 Conductors / Network Cables 
2.10.1 Unless otherwise noted, all conductors and grounds shall be stranded copper.   
2.10.2 The minimum conductor size shall be #16 AWG for AC control circuits, #14 AWG for (AC or DC) 
power circuits and #18 AWG for DC control circuits (where applicable) (This does not apply to 
premolded internal cables). The minimum conductor size for motor starter power wiring shall be #12 
AWG.  
2.10.3 All cables and premolded cables shall cover the amperage requirement / load of the application, 
please refer to the next table: 
 
2.10.4 Conductors shall be type MTW in control panels and THHN in conduit raceways. All conductors 
shall have thermoplastic insulation rated at 600 volts, 90 °C.  
2.10.5 Extra flexible wire shall be used between any door mounted components and the back panel 
mounted components with sufficient slack and spiral wrapping around all conductors to prevent 
pinching (MTW wire and THHN multiconductor). 
2.10.6 All cables ampacity shall be based on the table 310.16 of NEC (NFPA 70) environmental 
temperature (30°C). (Next picture is a reference only, please refere to latest copy of NEC) 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page20 
 
2.10.7 All local requirement or local authority (AHJ) requirements at the area shall be applied. 
2.10.8 All wire bundles within an electrical panel shall be bundled in a neat and professional way.  
2.10.9 Wire ties or spiral wrap shall be used when requires.  
2.10.10 Wires in wire ducts shall be of the correct length extra wire cannot be allowed in wire ducts. 
2.10.11 No tape shall be left on wire bundles inside of conduits or wire ducts. 
2.10.12 All overhead ladder style cable trays shall at least be 2.1 meters above the floor level. 
2.10.13 All overhead cable trays shall be Ladder type. 
2.10.14 All cable ducts below 2.1 meters shall be fully enclosed to protect the conductors within. (Trench, 
floor level cable trays, conduits, etc…) 
2.10.14.1 All floor level cable trays shall have heavy duty non slip covers (grip tape or diamond plate). 
2.10.14.2 Cable trays shall use a Unistrut to separate them from the floor. 
2.10.14.3 Cable trays close possible high damage locations shall use a heavy duty plate 1/8” cover (Ex. 
Close to fork truck pathways, or a risk to a part falling into the cable tray) 
2.10.15 Integrator shall apply all supplier guidelines for routing cables. 
2.10.16 Metalsa shall approve the routing for the cables.  
2.10.17 Devices that their cables need to be routed on fences shall have a Unistrut tray with its cover for 
routing them. Any deviation need approval of Metalsa.  
2.10.18 Unistruts exposed to welding spatter shall use the Metal type (Plastic type not allowed). 
 
 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page21 
2.10.20 Control and communication wires shall run in trays separated with the correct shielding separator 
from welding and power cables. The supplier shall ensure that there is no electromagnetic noise in the 
control and communication cables, for the way that the cables are routed. 
        
 
2.10.21 Moving wires on the floor or exposed to damage shall be routed through metallic flex cable track. 
2.10.22 Plastic flex cable track shall be use if they are not exposed to any possible damage. 
2.10.23 Cable Reel could be used in Press Mobil bolster applications with Metalsa approval. 
 
2.10.24 “SO” Cord shall not be used in control, unless approved by Metalsa. 
 
2.10.25 All part present sensors, actuator sensors, Robot Mounted Sensors, and IO Link quick connect 
cables that are exposed to damage shall be considered with a  sacrificial wire. The Length of the 
sacrificial wire is determined by the exposure of the cable in the work area (most of the times it is a 3 
feet / 1 meter cable).  
2.10.26 Multi-conductor cable shall meet local requirements (UL in US, CSA in Canada, etc..). 
2.10.27 Every multi-conductor wire used shall have all its conductors numbered, include a ground 
conductor in green/yellow color. 
 
2.11  Conductor Identification 
2.11.1 All control, power and network cables inside cabinets shall be labeled at both ends with non-
conductive and permanent printed labels.  
2.11.2 All control, power and network cables outside cabinets shall be labeled and protected at both ends 
with non-conductive and permanent printed labels.  
2.11.3 All labels shall follow Metalsas approved wiring diagrams nomenclature. 
2.11.4 Wires connected to programmable controller I/O shall be identified using the PLC I/O Tag Naming 
Convention (ex. I_015.14) or as otherwise specified by Metalsa.

2.13  Field wireable connector 
2.13.1 Approved steel clamps are Parker CL-9 for sensor cables 
2.13.2 Parker CL-9 shall be used in pneumatic hoses when more than 2 hoses are being routed from the 
valve manifold. 
2.13.3 Rexroth T-Clamps shall be used for routing hoses into specific actuator. 
2.13.4  
2.13.5 Field wireable connectors are prohibited on every type of cable, special cases require Metalsa 
consent. 
 
2.14 Splices  
2.14.1 Splices in panels or junction boxes requires a written Metalsa’s consent.  
2.14.2 Splices in conduits or fittings are prohibited.  
2.14.3 Splices and T’s in a cable tray are prohibited, if there is a need of a splice in a cable tray, Metalsa 
shall approve it. 
 
2.14.4 Any splices and T’s shall have a lamicoid indicating the physical location that cross reference with 
the electrical drawings. 
2.14.5 Splices shall be made with crimp type splice lugs and a wire marker provided on both sides of the 
splice. 
2.14.6 Where cables run through panel walls inside an enclosure.  
 
2.15 Enclosure external components 
2.15.1 Any push button or selector switch shall have no more 2 stacks of contact blocks.  
2.15.2 All pilot lamps shall be NEMA 13 construction and shall fit 30mm diameter pushbutton hole. 
2.15.3 Legend plates with switch/pushbutton shall be labeled with the function.

3. ENVIROMENTAL CONDITIONS OF DEVICES 
3.1 Temperature 
3.1.1 Enclosure working temperature calculation shall be done. 
3.1.2 Cooling system shall be installed if the calculation of the enclosure working temperature requires it. 
3.1.3 All enclosures operating and nonoperating temperature shall be within the range of the manufacturer 
recommendation of all the devices in the enclosure. Needs to be review and approved by Metalsa prior 
to build. 
3.1.4 Cooling systems (Heat exchanger, Air conditioner or fans) and Heat systems (Strip heaters, Heat 
exchanger) must meet the dust or metal dust environment and shall be approved by Metalsa. 
3.1.4.1 If a cooling system is required, a temperature sensor to monitor the temperature shall be 
included. 
3.1.4.2 Cooling system shall give status feedback to the control system. 
3.1.5 Cooling system shall supply dry non condensing air. 
3.1.6 All enclosures operating and nonoperating temperature shall consider the region ambient 
temperature.  
3.1.7 If operating and nonoperating enclosure temperature is outside of the manufacturer recommendation, 
a cooling system shall be installed to maintain the operating and nonoperating range at the point of use. 
3.1.8 Fans shall not be installed over panels or enclosures without prior approval by Metalsa.   
3.1.9 Fans shall maintain positive pressure in the enclosure.   
3.1.10 Fans shall be internally mounted unless approved by Metalsa. 
3.1.11 Fans finger guards shall be used. 
3.1.12 Inside cabinet air circulating fans (It does not bring air from outside the cabinet) shall be used to 
reduce inside cabinet temperature if the temperature compensation is the required. 
3.1.13 Outside air shall not be introduced into any enclosure for purposes of cooling without consent from 
Metalsa. 
3.1.14 Cooling systems shall be controlled by a thermostat or Metalsa approved substitute. 
3.1.15 Air conditioners shall not be mounted on top of enclosures. 
3.2 Humidity and liquids 
3.2.1 Enclosure working humidity calculation shall be done. 
3.2.2 Humidity sensor shall be included if the process requires it or ambient humidity is very high on the 
region. 
3.2.3 Internal cabinet humidity shall be non condensing. 
3.2.4 Water cooling system shall have a humidity sensor to prevent condensing. 
3.3 Dust 
3.3.1 If an air intake cooling system is used, a filter or system to prevent dust intake shall be provided to 
remove all dust, fibers and foreign material. 
3.3.2 Particle size of dust shall be consider in order to select the correct filter micron size. 
3.3.3 Intake air shall be at the bottom of the cabinet with at least a 2 feet distance from the floor. 
3.4 Vibration and shock 
3.4.1 Devices shall not be mounted in a machine with vibration or shock without prior approval by Metalsa 
3.4.2 Devices exposed to Vibration or shock shall be rated for that application. 
3.4.3 Terminal blocks exposed to vibration shall be spring type. 
3.4.4 All hydraulic/pneumatic/electrical piping shall be designed to minimize/eliminate shock/vibration.  

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page26 
3.4.5 All quick connectors or hartings exposed to vibration shall be designed to withstand long term 
shock/vibration without failure. 
3.4.6 Power tracks shall be designed for the velocity and radius according to the machine. 
3.4.7 Cable/hoses shall be specified to meet the velocity and radius requirements. 
3.4.8 Cable/hoses shall be specified to maximize service life. 
3.4.9 Power tracks shall be designed considering separators to avoid abrasion and cable/hose movement 
inside the power track. 
3.4.10 
 
3.4.11 Fittings/Splices shall not been used inside the power track, it shall be a continuos run from the in 
and out of the power track. 
3.4.12 On all machinery all devices shall meet environmental and machine conditions to maximize service 
life. 
3.5 Electromagnetic radiation EMR 
3.5.1 Needs to be discussed with a subject matter expert. (TBD) 
4. SAFETIES GOOD PRACTICES 
4.1 Safety requirements shall comply with the specifications of the Metalsa “Global safety requirements 
standard” and “Risk Assessment practice” chapters. 
4.2 These good practices of this chapter shall be use unless otherwise specified in the risk assessment.  
4.3 Robotic stations with operator interaction shall use DCS Speed and Cartesian Checks. 
4.4 On Robots with ESTOP signals over Ethernet/IP, the safety controller shall be able to detect loss of 
communications (controller shutdown). When that situation occurs Robot shall stop in place (E-Stop) and 
PLC that controls over Robot shall ensure communication before reenabling station / cell functionality. 
4.5 Status of all safety devices shall be displayed on dedicated “Safeties” HMI screen(s). (Only applicable if 
station / machine has HMI). 
4.6 Remote or Flex I/O panels shall use 1734-AENTR or 1734-AENT, 1734-IB8S and 1734-OB8S point I/O for 
safety control or 1791 CompactBlock (communication shall be Ethernet) Safety Modules. (1791 red 
modules) or Armor Point I/O or Turck Safety Block (Section 10.3 Master Modules I/O, Field Devices 
manual) 
4.7 1734 Point I/O devices shall be used only when inputs or outputs exceeds the capabilities of 1791 red 
modules (For example analog inputs) or there is required modularity for future inputs and outputs required. 
4.8 All safety gate plugs shall have mechanical override from inside fence.  
4.9 All motors shall have a way to disconnect motor power with a safety circuit. 
4.9.1 Motor with safety contactors 
4.9.2 Motor with drives with safe option 
4.9.3 Motor with drives and disconnect switch 
4.10 Safety device shall be connected directly to Safety Inputs. (Ex. Not to have hardwire daisy chain of e-
stops). If supplier suggest other option Metalsa consent required. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page27 
 
4.10.1 Where applies, safety device inputs to PLC shall use “Pulse Test” Common Connection. 
4.11 If a stand-alone station is inside or its part of an operation, not working independently, that device shall be 
part of the safety chain of the entire operation. (Example: If an e-stops pressed in the stand alone station, 
that device shall stop the entire operation) 
4.12 Any e-stop of the station shall stop the complete station. 
4.13 Any e-stop shall block the station or zone in which it is connected and located.  
4.13.1 Any equipment that is in the zone, station or work area shall be analyzed to be included in the 
devices that gets affected by that e-stop. 
4.14 Station Access request 
4.14.1 All safety gates shall have an interlock device. 
4.14.2 All machines with processes that requires to stop prior to access the cell shall have an Access 
request button or device to stop the machine in a safe state. 
4.14.3 All gates that does not have a Access request shall be approved by Metalsa. 
4.14.4 All Access request device that have a process that needs a way to keep energies while the person 
is in the station to make adjustments shall have a key selector switch, for the selection of the 
Teach/Run Mode, unless approved by Metalsa. (Example: Assembly robotic stations reteach) 
4.14.5 The Teach/Run Mode signals shall be connected to safety rated inputs. 
4.14.5.1 Access request Run Mode: Allows the operation to work in automatic, manual or Dry Cycle 
mode, under normal conditions. 
4.14.5.2 Access request Teach Mode: Allows the operation to retain specific energies that allows the 
capability to make adjustments in the machine. Risk assessment analysis is required to not 
generate an unsafe condition in this mode. 
4.15  Pneumatics 
4.15.1 Blue hose shall be use for extend cylinders and gray or black hose for retract. 
4.15.2 Red hose shall be use for feed after PO Check valves  
4.15.3 PO Check valves shall have a way to manually or automatic release the pressure on the lock side 
unless requested and approved by Metalsa. 
4.16 Control Relays 
4.16.1 Shall be DIN rail mountable unless approved by Metalsa. 
4.16.2 Control relays shall be mounted vertically with print always in upright position, unless approved by 
Metalsa. 
4.16.3 Pin socket style relays shall have retainer clip (no conductive material) or equivalent. 
4.16.4 Refer to “01_ControlsSpecs_PartList” for Approved Control Relays. 
 
 
 
 
4.17  Safety Relays 
4.17.1 Shall be DIN rail mountable. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page28 
4.17.2 Shall be 24vdc. 
4.17.3 Safety relays shall be mounted vertically with print always in upright position. 
4.17.4 Safety Relays shall be used only to interact with safety PLC, they shall not have any internal 
programming required to function, deviation shall need Metalsa approval. 
4.17.5 Transfers in stations requiring operator interaction during motion shall be safety rated. (The required 
level shall be defined by the Risk Assestment).  
4.17.6 Refer to “01_ControlsSpecs_PartList” for Approved Safety Relays  
 
4.18 Safety Circuits 
4.18.1 All machinery guards or barriers used to protect personnel that can not be removed without the use 
of tools, shall be equipped with an approved safety interlock device.  This device shall conform to 
current and applicable safety regulations. 
4.18.2 All Emergency Stops shall have dual channel, indicator light, maintained position and safety rated. 
4.18.3 Any operator station that has automatic movement shall have a safety rated detection device to 
detect the personnel inside the fixture. 
4.18.4 All safety circuit ratings shall be determined by the risk assessment. 
4.18.5 All individual equipments shall meet the station safety circuit rating determined by the risk 
assessment. 
4.18.6 If a risk assessment is not implemented and was approved by EHSS Metalsa Team. Metalsa shall 
specify the minimum category of the safety circuit. 
5. GROUND SYSTEM 
 
5.1 Equipment and machinery grounding 
5.1.1 Welding ground shall comply with the JKC Manual Requirements Standard 
5.1.2 
 
5.1.3 Physical Electrical earth ground shall be used (Either by Ground rod or building column). 
5.1.4 Physical Electrical Grounding shall be labeled. 
5.1.5 All devices shall have a ground or be daisy chained to a grounding point. 
5.1.6 All grounding shall comply with the authority having jurisdiction (AHJ). 
 
5.2 Panel Grounding 
5.2.1 A common grounding bus with provisions to bond to an external ground system such as the building 
ground and/or grounding rod shall be provided.   
5.2.2 All devices that require grounding shall be grounded in accordance with the manufacturer's 
specifications. 
5.2.3 The path to ground from all distribution equipment and apparatus shall be permanent, continuous and 
in accordance with the authority having jurisdiction (AHJ). 
6. MOTORS, STARTERS, CONTACTORS AND DRIVES 
6.1 Motors 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page29 
6.1.1 All motors of 1 hp or greater shall meet energy efficiency requirements per the Energy policy Act 
(EPACT) or the authority having jurisdiction (AHJ). Metalsa shall approve special purpose motors that 
do not meet these efficiencies. 
6.1.2 Motors shall be the highest efficiency that is available from a manufacturer. 
6.1.3 All motors shall be totally enclosed fan cooled (TEFC) unless approved by Metalsa. 
6.1.4 Motors for use with AC drives shall be inverter duty rated and high efficiency rated. 
 
6.2 Motor Starters and Contactors in Applications other than Motor Control Centers 
6.2.1 Motor Starters shall only be used in place of VFD with Metalsa’s consent. 
6.2.2 IEC type preferred. 
6.2.3 Shall be DIN rail mountable unless approved by Metalsa. 
6.2.4 Shall have at least 1 auxiliary contact for status to PLC. 
6.2.5 Shall have 24vdc coils.  
6.2.5.1 Motor Starter requiring different 24vdc coils requires Metalsa´s approval. 
6.2.6 Motor Starters shall have electronic overloads. 
6.2.7 Combination starters shall be used in single motor circuits only with Metalsa’s consent. 
6.2.8 **add picture** 
6.2.9 The use of manual starters is prohibited unless Metalsa authorized in writing.  
6.2.10 Starters shall be mounted within the system enclosure provided with a lockable disconnect for the 
entire system. 
6.2.11 Each motor starter shall have a dedicated circuit breaker. 
6.2.12 Motor starters / contactors shall be 3-pole, 600v, kW/horsepower rated with 3-pole manual reset 
overload relay. 
6.2.13 Overload relays shall be adjusted depending on the motor name plate data. 
6.2.14 Motors of 75 HP/55 kW and above shall be provided with reduced voltage starter / contactor.  The 
reduced voltage starter/contactor shall be solid-state with bypass contactor. 
6.2.15  All motors shall be continuous duty type. 
6.2.16  Wye/Delta motors starters shall be approved by Metalsa. 
6.2.17 If applicable, motor disconnects shall have a warning tag/indicator for capacitors discharged. 
6.2.18 Refer to “01_ControlsSpecs_PartList” for Approved Motor Starters / Contactors / Overloads. 
6.2.19 R/C networks and surge suppressers shall be used in all motor starters or contactors that introduce 
an inductive load to the controls circuit. 
6.3 Motor Control Centers  
6.3.1 Allen Bradley (Bulletin 2100) NEMA 12 motor control centers shall be utilized in multiple motor 
applications unless otherwise specified by Metalsa.  The minimum of requirements for motor control 
centers are delineated below. 
6.3.1.1 Minimum requirements for motor control center (Allen Bradley 2100): 
6.3.1.1.1 NEMA enclosuretype:  12 
6.3.1.1.2 Depth:  15" 
6.3.1.1.3 Paint:  standard 
6.3.1.1.4 Line voltage:  480v 3 phase 60hz 
6.3.1.1.5 Connection:  fusible disconnect, (main lugs only with Metalsa's consent) 
6.3.1.1.6 Entry:  top or bottom  (as required) 
6.3.1.1.7 Horizontal bus:  800A tinned copper 
6.3.1.1.8 Vertical bus:  300A copper 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page30 
6.3.1.1.9 Bus bracing:  42,000 AIC symmetrical (Or as required by the local application available 
short circuit current) 
6.3.1.1.10 Ground bus:  1/4" x 1" no plating (bottom) 
6.3.1.1.11 Door nameplates:  engraved lamecoid-white w/black letters 
6.3.1.1.12 Master nameplate:  engraved lamecoid-white w/black letters 
6.3.2 When horizontal bus rating exceeds 800 amps; vertical buss rating shall increase to 400 amps. 
6.3.3 All disconnect switches on motor control centers shall be provided with a normally open auxiliary 
contact wired to terminals to indicate the status of the switch. 
6.3.4 All motor control centers shall be ordered and shipped in single sections and include all necessary 
hardware for connecting together in the field. 
6.3.5 All motor control centers shall provide a minimum of one pare full space provision, plus a full space 
provision for each two sections of motor control center. Buckets shall be arranged to use the MCC’s 
space to the greatest advantage, by arranging unused spaces into their largest group. Half spaces shall 
not be considered as space provisions. 
6.3.6 All drives shall shall operator interface module mounted with a Lexan viewing window. 
6.3.7 Electrical contractor shall provide a concrete mounting pad.  Pad shall be 3.5” high and extend 1” 
from all sides of the MCC. 
6.3.8 All PLC controlled coils shall have surge suppressors.  
6.3.9 All sections shall have a green light to indicate the motor starter is engaged. 
6.3.10 MCC’s shall use Ethernet IP communications. 
6.3.10.1 On MCC’s containing a PLC, a “hand/off/auto” switch shall be provided. 
6.3.10.2 On MCC’s containing a PLC, the following conditions need to be monitored. 
Disconnect position 
Remote Disconnect position 
Starter position 
Over Load Relay 
 
6.4 Variable Speed Drives 
6.4.1 VFD’s are motor control preference.  
6.4.2 Line reactors and isolation transformers shall be installed before frequency drives or servomotors 
over 5 HP. For drives / servomotors under 5 HP, a line reactor and/or isolation transformer will only be 
required if the manufacturer or facility requires it. 
6.4.3 All drives shall have a diagnostic interface. If the drive has a programming module, it shall be 
supplied. 
6.4.4 Ethernet/IP is the control communication preferred, for a different communication protocol, Metalsa 
approval is required. 
6.4.5 All motor drives shall have a “Safe Off” option. 
6.4.6 Refer to “01_ControlsSpecs_PartList” for The approved AC Drives & approved Servo Drives

10. POWER & FREES / OVERHEAD CONVEYORS 
10.1 Interface 
10.1.1 Ethernet IP. 
10.1.2 IO Link Distributed IO shall be used. 
10.1.3 ON Machine Module IP67 1732E  
10.2 Should have extended / returned sensors for all cylinders. 
10.3 Should have ‘Carrier Clear of Stop’ at all load / unload stops. 
10.4 Stops  
10.4.1 Shall have both extended and returned sensors. 
10.4.2 Valves shall be 2 position, single acting, spring return. 
10.4.3 Shall have product on carrier sensing at all load / unload stops. 
10.4.4 Load and Unload Stops shall have mechanical means of trapping product during robot load / unload 
sequences.  
10.5 Carriers  
10.5.1 Shall have positive locator’s cylinders at load / unload stops. 
10.5.2 Valves shall be 2 position valves. 
10.5.3 Overtravel detection must be used. Hardware sensors must be installed 
10.5.4 Automatic carrier identification shall be used for part tracking 
11. AUTOMATIC/MANUAL OPERATION 
11.1 All equipment shall have an automatic cycle and a manual cycle with an operator device who allow each 
motion to be operated separately and can facilitate the setup and maintenance operations. All HMI 
enclosures shall be equipped with a “System Auto Mode” pushbutton with a pilot amber light, “System 
Manual Mode” push button with green pilot light, and “System Control Power On” button with white pilot 
light. 
11.2 System Reset Non Illuminated Push Button 
11.3 When manual mode is working safety features cannot be compromised. 
 
12. ROBOTICS APPLICATIONS 
12.1 Robotic Installations shall comply with federal, state, and local codes as well as: 
12.1.1 ANSI/RIA r15.06 (Latest version) 
12.1.2 ISO10218 (Latest version) 
12.2 Robotic equipment shall not be electrically or mechanically modified from manufacturer’s configuration 
without Metalsa´s approval.  

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page33 
12.3 Robotic equipment shall not be modified in a way that would void the warranty of the equipment from the 
supplier without Metalsa´s and Manufacturer´s approval. 
12.4 Installation of robotic equipment shall be in accordance with manufacturer's specifications and 
recommendations. 
12.5 Metalsa shall specify the robotic manufacturer. 
12.6 Metalsa shall approve robot model. 
12.7 Metalsa shall supply robot and plc program templates to define the robotic program structures (Refer to 
07 – Robot Specifications Global Standard).  Supplier shall not swap over from template without Metalsa´s 
approval. 
12.8 All External I/O cables & Comms which connect from PLC to robot controller shall have quick 
disconnects. 
12.9 Robots shall communicate by a control protocol (Refer to 01 Part list – protocol section) to the PLC and 
its peripherals. Metalsa´s approval needed for protocol selection. 
12.10 PLC shall be controller and Robot shall be peripheral device. 
12.11 It´s acceptable for Robot controllers to have peripheral devices. 
12.12 HMI or Teach shall have the following robot functions: 
12.12.1 Robot control (Servo On/System Ready). 
  
12.12.2 Mode Status (Teach/Auto indicators). 
12.12.3 Offset capabilities (for Brackets robots only). 
12.12.4 Program start and hold functions. 
12.12.5 Torch Cleaner Status / Test Functions. 
12.12.6 Go to maintenance(service)/tip change position. 
12.12.7 Go to G0 axis/initial(home) position. 
12.13 Incoming power for all robot controllers shall be determined by the country voltage standard and 
approved by Metalsa. 
12.14 Robot teach pendant cable shall be long enough to be able to reach the robot to make in a safe way any 
robot reteach. 
12.15 Fence pass through can be used for robot teach pendants to reach the robot reteach location. 
12.16 Fence pass through, guarding and barriers shall be evaluated in the risk assestment. 
12.17 If a robot controller uses a teach mode key, then the robot controller enable panel shall be mounted in 
close proximity of robot’s closest entrance point or the location specified in the Metalsa standard cell 
design layout. 
12.18 Robots shall not have the ability to select a teach speed above 250mm/sec unless requested and 
approved by Metalsa. 
12.19 Risk assessment analysis shall include all the robots with the ability to select a teach speed above 
250mm/sec 
12.20 Robots shall have safety communication by an Ethernet protocol. 
12.21 Robots that does not support communication by an ethernet protocol shall have integrated safety 
controls, or a safety module remotely mounted in controller to interface with safety controller. 
12.22 All robots in a given fixture shall be setup to share relative frame directions to fixture work piece.   
12.23 All robots shall have collision detection software if available. 
12.24 All robots shall have means of automatically backing up programs and configuration parameters on a 
robot local memory and by FPT 
12.25 Robot controllers shall not be on the ground; controllers shall be on overhead mezzanines, when a 
mezzanine does not exists a base shall be included instead. 
12.26 Any mechanical robot unit, external axis and gearboxes payload shall not exceed the manufacturer’s 
specified robot capacity payload calculation chart unless approved by the robot manufacturer and gearbox 
manufacturer. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page34 
12.27 Robot , external axis and gearboxes payload charts shall be done on every robot and be validated by 
the robot manufacturer and gearbox manufacturer. (Not to exceed more than 80% of payload, if more is 
needed, a Metalsa approval is required) 
12.28 Material Handler Applications: 
12.28.1 End effector I/O shall be controlled directly by robot controller.  I/O, devices and communication 
status shall be conveyed to the PLC for operator screens, troubleshooting, etc.  
12.28.2 Ethernet/IP devices or Robot I/O shall be use to control the end effector. 
12.28.3 Material Handlers shall have dedicated shut off valve and pressure switches. 
12.28.4 I/O shall be mounted into End effector. In case the I/O and devices are exposed to welding, it shall 
be properly guarded (Refer to Field devices  and tooling standards) 
12.28.5 All end effector outputs shall be manipulated from the robot teach pendant. 
12.29 When Material Handlers requiring tool change out shall utilize ATI quick change couplers. 
12.30 End effector quick change couplers shall connect all electrical, pneumatics or any energy source 
through the coupler. Specific Style is to be based on application approved by Metalsa. 
12.31 ATI Lock / Unlock outputs shall be controlled using safe reference position. 
12.32 Material handlers robots end effector designs shall give the values for the tool center position (TCP) . 
12.33 Vacuum Equipment shall not be used, if it is absolutely necessary, requires an approval by Metalsa. 
12.34 Any station that have Trunnion table, requires all the robots (material handling or welding robots) who 
interact with the station shall be in a safe position while the station is in movement. (Using DCS in Fanuc 
robots) 
12.35 Integrator shall include Metalsa IO (Karel) in all Fanuc robots with the following functionalities: (For other 
brands and equivalent functionality shall be used) 
12.35.1 Daily autobackups 
12.35.2 Clamp / actuators and sensors mapping at a single location. 
12.35.3 Automatic loading of DI and DO comments 
12.35.4 Position Offset function 
12.35.5 Palletizing 
12.35.6 Safe position validation to close or open clamps / cilinders / actuators 
12.36 Integrator shall include and configure Inteligent interference check (IIC) and Dual check safety (DCS) for 
all Fanuc robots with the following functionalities: (For other brands and equivalent functionality shall be 
used) 
12.36.1 Prevention of colitions with external axis with robot arms. 
12.36.2 Prevention of colitions between robot arms. 
12.37 Robot name Stenciling shall be considered by integrator:

13. PROGRAMABLE CONTROLLERS 
13.1 Metalsa shall approve the particular type of Allen Bradley Control-Logix or Compact-Logix processor, 
safety partner, local related l and remote I/O cards. 
13.2 Supplier shall follow the brand options listed on the “11 - Equipment Standard List V1” document. 
13.3 Metalsa shall approve the selected PLC brand at the beginning of the project. 
13.4 Metalsa shall approve any part not listed on the “11 - Equipment Standard List V1” document. 
13.5 Programmable controllers shall be used instead of the electromechanical controls unless Metalsa 
approves it. 
13.6 Metalsa shall supply PLC and HMI / Touch Screen program templates to define the program and interface 
structures.  Supplier shall not make any change from template without Metalsa approvals. 
13.7 The required spare shall  meet the following list at install while process is cycling: 
13.7.1 Inputs and outputs spare capacity  25% 
13.7.2 Processor communication spare capacity 25% 
13.7.3 Scan time shall have a maximum of 75ms. 
13.7.4 Rack spare capacity 25% 
13.7.5 Memory spare capacity 25% 
13.7.6 Safety memory spare capacity 25% 
13.7.7 Motion controls spare capacity 25% 
13.8 The required spare shall meet the following list at all times in operation while process is cycling: 
13.8.1 Inputs and outputs spare capacity  10% 
13.8.2 Processor communication spare capacity 10% 
13.8.3 Scan time shall have a maximum of 100ms. 
13.8.4 Rack spare capacity 10% 
13.8.5 Memory spare capacity 10% 
13.8.6 Safety memory spare capacity 10% 
13.8.7 Motion controls spare capacity 10% 
13.9 All processors and modules revisions and series shall be approved by Metalsa. 
13.10 All processors and modules software and firmware version shall be approved by Metalsa in the Design 
phase. 
13.11 PLC Logic must not be password protected, security must not be enabled and source protection shall be 
disabled. 
13.12 Metalsa shall have access to all the programs during the building and start-up. 
13.13 The processor shall contain standard and safety logic on the same PLC, if the standard and safety 
needs to be on two processors, it shall be approved by Metalsa. 
13.14 For rack style processors the safety PLC and the partner shall be on the first position after the power 
supply. 
13.15 Any Non-Allen PLC manufacturer provided Add-On Instruction and Add-On profiles not shared by 
Metalsa shall not be encrypted or proprietary and shall be visible, unless approved by Metalsa 
13.15.1 Any Metalsa shared Add-On Instruction and Add-On profile shall not be changed unless approved 
by Metalsa. 
13.16 All safety Add-On instructions shall be provided by the manufacturer of the PLC or provided by Safety 
Component OEM, it shall never be altered. 
13.16.1 Any non PLC manufacturer provided Add-On instructions shall have the validation of TUV. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page37 
13.17 While it is encouraged to use Add-On instructions (approved) for specific functions, Add- On instructions 
shall not be used to perform a general sequential logic. 
13.18 Alias Tags shall not be used, unless approved by Metalsa. 
13.19 IP address range, gateway and structure shall be provided by Metalsa. 
13.20 All I/O shall be appropriately labeled including unused I/O. 
13.21 All In-cabinet I/O shall be wired to terminal blocks including unused I/O.
