14. HUMAN MACHINE INTERFACE 
14.1 HMI shall be located considering the safety distance to actuate any device. 
14.2 HMI shall provide direct sightline to the fixture in order to avoid manual operation without supervision. 
14.2.1 Any circunstante that does not meet this requirement needs an agreement between Metalsa and 
supplier on the functionality on how to actuate the devices in a safe matter. 
14.2.2 If the HMI is not in a direct sightline for the operator shall use an auditive alarm. 
14.3 All HMI shall be placed on a robotic station and every manual station with more than 4 valves and/or 10 
units (Clamps & Cylinders). 
14.4 All HMI placement and quantity shall be agreed on design. 
14.4.1 All subassembly stations shall have at least 1 HMI 
14.4.2 All mainline and stubs zones shall have at least 1 HMI 
14.4.3 All standalone conveyor systems shall have at least 1 HMI 
14.4.4 All presses shall have at least 1 HMI 
14.4.5 All coil lines shall have at least 1 HMI 
14.5 All the screens in the HMI shall be in English and local language, it shall have a switch function of the 
languages. 
14.6 It is prohibited that the HMI Enclosure have a 110VAC/220VAC contact for any device. 
14.6.1 110VAC/220VAC outled shall be within 3 feet of HMI enclosure. 
14.6.2 This does not apply to HMI mounted on MCP/System enclosure. 
14.7 All HMI enclosures shall have an RFID reader compatible with Metalsa’s identification card. 
14.7.1 RFID reader shall be agreed with Metalsa on Design Phase.  
14.8 Every HMI shall have a red light / Stacklight to visually indicate that the station has an alarm. 
14.9 HMI enclosure shall be mounted in a fix stand, actuated arm or a rail mounted. 
14.9.1 Fix Stand Picture 
14.9.2 Actuated arm picture 
14.9.3 Rail mounted picture 
14.10 All HMI enclosures shall have the following pushbuttons 
14.10.1 Control power reset (Safeties reset) 
14.10.2 Alarm reset (Standard reset) 
14.11 All HMI enclosures shall have an ESTOP. 
15. NETWORK DESIGN 
15.1 Supplier shall submit the network design drawing for approval by Metalsa. 
15.2 Metalsa shall specify the IP address range and VLANS of the network. 
15.2.1 VLAN numbers shall be approved by the Metalsa IT department. 
15.3 Network shall be design and install to meet ODVA and device manufacturer. 
15.4 Network protocol is specified in the Devices and Part List documentation. 
15.5 Machine interlocks (not separate interlocks) shall be via Network protocol, any other safety interlock shall 
be aproved by Metalsa.

18. INDUSTRY 4.0 SUPPLIER OT REQUIREMENTS 
 
18.1 Policies for digital solutions providers 
18.2 Devices/Controllers: 
Most use cases for controllers can fall in these three categories, category “A” is prioritized, “B” is 
possible, and “C” is not recommended unless special conditions exist: 
18.2.1 Categories 
18.2.1.1 Data already available in Metalsa´s controllers or devices: Use of existing hardware and 
infrastructure shall be prioritized, also use of existing data or new data derived from the processing 
of internal existing tags. For this, process automation shall be involved. The supplier shall indicate 
all data requirements. 
18.2.1.2 Data to be integrated into Metalsa´s controllers or devices: Use of new I/O or tags integrated to 
Metalsa´s controllers. The supplier shall specify all data requirements and usually lead the 
deployment and programming. 
18.2.1.3 Data to be extracted through separate controllers or devices: Use of new I/O and Controllers. 
For this, all the standard documentation and compliance will be required (drawings, labeling, 
cabling, etc. See controls standard). All should be approved by process automation and OT Lead. 
 
18.2.2 Required for all cases: 
18.2.2.1 All installation shall follow the current Metalsa Controls Standard. 
18.2.2.2 The I4.0 and process automation leads shall be involved. 
18.2.2.3 All Sensors, actuators, controllers, cameras and other devices interacting with the 
manufacturing process or ingesting data from it shall be hosted in the plant controls network. For 
this, special static addresses shall be requested to Service Desk by the process automation 
champion. 
18.2.3 Gateways / Data Ingestion: 
18.2.3.1 If the application needs to consume data from devices in a production/controls network, it shall 
consume them from a Metalsa OPC UA server or a secure Gateway/Proxy server located in the 
Enterprise Network. This server will connect directly to the devices and through the different 
networks to expose the data to the supplier OPC UA Client or to the supplier cloud clients 
 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page43 
18.2.3.2 A secure solution shall be deployed, for this, use of Metalsa Gateways is enforced. The current 
gateway product is Kepware.  
18.2.3.3 Additional Kepware servers will have to be considered depending on the application and 
physical location, network domains, for getting data and hopping between production and enterprise 
networks, including VMs, licensing, etc. 
18.2.3.4 An alternative use case involving supplier servers for these purposes is not allowed unless a 
deviation is approved by the automation, OT and iSecurity Leads. 
18.2.3.5 Any application sending or receiving data through internet shall be hosted in Metalsa 
Enterprise zone. 
18.2.3.6 If supplier servers are needed, it is recommended to host it in Metalsa VMs. If Supplier 
requires special Hardware, location will have to be clarified with OT and IT leads. And device will 
have to be cleared by iSecurity team. 
18.2.3.7 The connection to the OPC UA Server will be done using a specific OPC UA endpoint 
provided by Metalsa. 
18.2.3.8 Also, OPC UA authentication shall be used: a specific username and password will be 
provided by metalsa. 
18.2.3.9 Security Policies to be used are: Basic256Sha256 Sign and Encrypt. If not available in the 
server, Basic256 Sign and Encrypt or Basic128Rsa15 Sign and Encrypt can be used. 
18.2.3.10 An OPC UA certified client shall be used or provide guarantee of compliance, since the 
Metalsa server provides services for other applications, it shall be guaranteed to not impair its 
performance. 
18.2.3.11 Data Integrity and security shall be achieved. 
18.2.3.12 Current data ingestion polling rate is 1 second. If faster rates are required, an Edge device 
can be installed and connected directly to the controller. All software and hardware requirements for 
this shall be covered by the supplier and comply with the policies in this document. 
18.2.3.13 All edge devices shall comply with latest Metalsa controls, IT and iSecurity standards. For 
this devices, turnkey access shall be provided to Metalsa and explicit I4.0 OT Lead approval is 
needed. 
18.2.3.14 Access to Metalsa´s controllers and devices shall be read only 
18.2.3.15 Access is available through Metalsa Gateway. Current Supported protocols are:

18.3 Policies for Original Equipment Manufacturers. 
18.3.1 General Policies  
18.3.1.1 Machine controller should be delivered as a turnkey project. The controller(s) & HMI programs 
and passwords should be delivered to metalsa. 
18.3.1.2 Machine should incorporate a program to generate all the ODiX required data & KPIs 
(production, quality, andon, process parameters, condition monitoring, etc.), this will be detailed in 
working sessions between Metalsa and Supplier. Supplier is responsible for programming the data 
needed. In some cases PLC & HMI programs are already developed and will be shared with the 
supplier. For details, reach automation lead or OT lead. 
18.3.1.3 In all cases, supplier should allow Metalsa the programming of new routines/programs in the 
controller to generate data for new digital manufacturing applications.  
18.3.1.4 When installed, all machine IP addresses should be integrated into Metalsa plant controls 
network. Static addresses or segments shall be requested from Metalsa. Communication to ODiX & 
MES servers in this network shall be guaranteed. 
18.3.1.5 Machine controllers and HMIs should comply with Metalsa Controls Standard, and should act 
as an OPC UA Server. If not, it should be compatible with a Ethernet based communication protocol 
supported by Kepware. For a full list visit: https://www.kepware.com/en-
us/products/kepserverex/suites/manufacturing-suite/  and consider only ethernet based. 
18.3.1.6 Remote access hardware and software for the machine is not recommended due to security 
concerns and if used, should be approved by the plant iSecurity, Network and OT Leads.

20. DOCUMENTATION 
20.1 The supplier shall submit assembly line as built documentation (electronical format) before shipment of 
the line to the receiving facility. 
20.2 All drawings shall be elaborated by the supplier and approved by Metalsa.  
20.3 Bill of material and equipment shall be approved by Metalsa during the designing phase. 
20.4 Before the final payment is agreed, the supplier shall submit to Metalsa final/reviewed “as built” 
documentation. 
20.5 During the next 90 days after the payment if there is some corrections to be done, the supplier shall 
update the documentation. 
20.6 Main Control Panel & Zone Panels shall have the corresponding hard copy of the drawings located inside 
of the panel. 
20.7 Drawings shall be inside a protected cover 
20.8 Any third party equipment purchased by the integrator shall have the drawings inside the panel. 
20.9 Any Robot, PLC, HMI, drive, industrial PC, periferiral or device programs, configurations or related 
programming structures or any source code developed by a supplier as part of contractual work for 
Metalsa, shall be property of Metalsa, it shall NOT be encrypted or rendered (uneditable) by Metalsa. 
20.10 All devices programs and configurations shall be delivered as a backup of the program to Metalsa.

networks.

21. SENSORS AND CORDSETS 
21.1 Cordsets and sensors      
21.1.1 All sensing devices shall use PNP wiring. 
21.1.2 All sensing devices shall be fitted with M12 male quick disconnect. 
21.1.3 Non field wireable connectors shall be used. 
21.1.4 Non test pulse sensors, limit switches, sensors without a light indicator or if the light indicator is 
hidden shall use a lighted cordset. 
21.1.5 Reed style cylinder position sensors are prohibited without Metalsa approval. 
21.1.6 Limit Switches and square prox’s are preferred method of part presence detection where precision 
detection is not required. 
21.1.7 Sensor range, type and size shall be properlly selected based on the process. 
21.1.8 Cylindicators that could make a risk of leaking air or oil if removed are prohibited unless approved 
by Metalsa.  
21.1.8.1 Example:
 
21.1.9 All cylinders shall indicate HOME and WORK positions unless approved by Metalsa. 
21.1.10 All splitters (pneumatic and electric) connections shall be identified on both ends and every 5 
meters in between. 
21.1.11 Indirect sensor (plunger) to detect part present shall be reviewed and approved by Metalsa. 
21.1.12 Indirect sensor to detect WORK/HOME position shall be considered as first option. 
21.1.13 PokaYokes bases shall be painted in sea green and Part Preset bases shall be yellow. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
21.1.14 6mm set screws shall be use in all sensor’s bushings. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page52 
 
21.1.15 Integrator shall include lamicoids for identification of Part present, pokayokes, and actuators. 
 
21.1.16 M12 cables used for IO LINK shall be white. 
21.1.17 M12 cables used for Safety devices shall be red. 
21.1.18 M12 cables used in high temperature applications shall be orange. 
21.1.19 Cables used for sensors and power supply shall be yellow. 
 
 
21.1.20 Photoelectric and Vision sensors shall be approved by Metalsa.  
21.1.21 Photoelectric and Vision sensors shall have a proper protection cover. (See”5.8.3 Protection for 
Vision Sensors in Welding”).

22. FIELD DEVICES PROTECTION 
22.1 Cordset cables 
22.1.1 Consider “sacrificial” cable for all cables that are not fixed or covered and exposed to damage (such 
as welding, motion, cutting, piercing).  
22.1.2 Sacrificial wire shall be easily accesable.  
22.2 Conduits 
 
22.2.1 Edge covers in Conduit and trays shall be consider preventing damage to hoses and cables. 
 
22.3 Sensor Protection 
22.3.1 Barrel type proximity switches shall not be mounted in slots for adjustment.  Adjustments should be 
made by means of adjustable mounting plates or adjustable actuators. 
22.3.2 Bushings and guards shall be use for all sensors. Integrator shall Refer to Guard Designs from 
Metalsa reference files: “Bushing and Guard Designs bundle”, adding the following protection designs: 
22.3.2.1 Block Sensor Guard 
22.3.2.2 Camera Guard 
22.3.2.3 M8 Bushing with Cable

22.3.2.6 M18 Bushing

22.3.2.8 WTB9 Laser Sensor Guard Type 1 
22.3.2.9 WTB9 Laser Sensor Guard Type 2

23.1.2 The election of the blocks is according to the application

1. General requirements 
1.1 Shall follow the recommendations from manufacturer.  
1.2 Operating temperature: 
1.2.1 Prior to using water as a coolant prior approval shall be obtained from Metalsa Engineering. 
1.2.2 Manifolds should be positioned to have line of sight with tooling/clamps if actuates. 
1.2.3 Aluminum manifolds are not permitted. 
1.2.4 Manifolds should have supply and return line shutoff valves. 
1.2.5  Consider the use of pilot check valves at both sides, to avoid forward or backward movements of 
actuators, with flux regulator valve and directional valves. 
1.2.6 Label of every valve shall be placed in the manifold block. 
1.3 The norm CETOP shall be used. 
1.4 Any manual valve shall be monitored with a prox to be sure its open/close. 
1.5 At the moment to integrate a hydraulic unit, shall be considerate the following components: 
1.5.1 Suction filter  
1.5.2 Return filter with differential pressure monitoring with visual indicator. 
 
1.5.3 Pressure filter with differential pressure monitoring with visual indicator. 
1.5.4 shall temperature, level, flow IO Link Sensors. 
1.5.5 Shall have I/O Link or Analog pressure switch per pressure line. 
1.5.6 A flow meter shall be used in all pump outlets. 
1.5.7 Filter sensors shall have monitoring function to prevent a disconnection. 
1.5.8 Shall be use resistance or heat sink depending to the weather (when the units are not isolated) 
1.5.9 The distance of the pump to the circuit shall be as straight as possible. 
1.5.10 Is recommendable than after a device that can be stop the flow use the EMA connections. 
1.5.11 Magnetic traps at Tank.  
1.5.12 Every Unit shall have their own recirculation pump. 
1.6 Servo hydraulic unit HPU shall be used unless approved by Metalsa. 
2. Safety good practices 
2.1 Safety requirements shall comply with the specifications of the Metalsa “Global safety requirements 
standard” and “Risk Assessment practice” chapters.

3. Diagrams 
3.1 The builder shall provide the preliminary hydraulic diagrams with bill of materials in the latest AutoCAD 
drawing format to METALSA for approval.  The approved data will be returned to the builder. The approval 
will be established prior to proceeding with the installation of the hydraulic components on the equipment. 
METALSA will not be responsible for any costs incurred by the builder prior to hydraulic approval. 
3.2 Spare part list shall also be included in the drawings. 
3.3 The diagrams and sketches used to build the hydraulic system including bill of material shall be supplied 
when METALSA request, diagrams or sketches have to illustrate the installation of hydraulic system may 
also be requested. 
3.4 The original and latest version of diagrams supplied according to ANSI standards shall be provided on 
memory sticks in the latest AutoCAD format with a METALSA title block. 
3.5 Final drawings shall include equipment sketches showing hydraulic, pneumatic. 
4. Fluid reservoirs and pumps: 
4.1 All hydraulic power units controlled by a PLC, shall have an alarm programmed regarding a setpoint of 
working hours for preventive maintenance purposes. 
4.2 All hydraulic power units that have stand-alone control shall be equipped with an hour meter for 
preventative maintenance purposes. 
4.3 Soft started shall be used in each motor. 
4.4 24 VDC coils shall be used. 
4.5 All hydraulic power units controlled by a PLC, the flow meter measurement shall be sended to the PLC.  
4.6 All hydraulic power units that have stand-alone control, the flow meter shall have a display.  
4.7 Tanks larger than 250 gallons shall have electronic leak detection interlocks 
4.8 Any manual ball valve shall be monitored via PLC. 
4.9 Automatic shutdown of hydraulic system equipment may be accomplished through the use of one of the 
following: 
4.9.1 Fire detector system or sprinkler water flow switch if required by safety guidelines. 
4.9.2 Oil reservoir liquid level switch interlocked with the oil pump.  
4.9.3 Oil temperature reach a high temperature shall shoutdown automatically. 
4.9.4 Pressure inside the system pass the safe limit it shall shoutdown automatically. 
4.10 LOW LEVEL SWITCH MUST BE SET AS TO NOT DAMAGE THE EQUIPMENT.  
4.11 Ensure that the recirculation pump always be working (even though the workstation it’s off). 
4.12 Oil temperature sensor shall trigger an alarm before reaching the temperature limit specified by the 
manufacturer of the oil and shall be approved by METALSA. 
4.13 For Servo units, when the oil reaches the High oil temperature an acknowledge button shall let you run 
the equipment no more than 10minutes. 
4.14 If during HPU design a separate cooling system if needed shall be added. 
4.15 If the facility where the hydraulic units is going to be installed, the weather temperature reaches below or 
equal to the minimum working temperature of the oil, resistors or heaters shall be used. 
 
5. Cylinders and pistons: 
5.1 All cylinders shall monitor work and home position detecting the component that is link to the rod (indirect 
sensing).

6. Valves 
6.1 All valves shall have be 43650 DIN electrical connectors. 
 
6.2 Valve Plug Forms shall be specified during Hydraulic System design. 
6.3 All valves shall be connected to a single port of an IO Link Configurable output blocks. 
6.4 The maximum Amps capacity of the IO Link Configurable Output Block shall not be exceeded. 
6.5 All directional valves shall have manual overrides. 
6.6 All directional valves shall use 24vdc solenoids. 
6.7 Proportional valves shall use 0-10vdc solenoids as preferred. 
6.7.1 If the process requires a different control of the solenoid 4-20mA shall be used. 
6.8 20% spare per manifold shall be provided. 
7. Pressure switches 
7.1 Real pressure signal (not use digital signal (on/off)) shall be used in the PLC.  
7.2 At the input connection of the station a pressure switch shall be considered. 
7.3 Critical process features shall be equipped with pressure switches.

1.1. Pressure requirements: 
1.1.1. The compressed air pressure in the main airline: 
Maximum 
120 psi 
Average 
85 psi

available. 
1.1.3. Special regulations for Kentucky state:  
1.1.3.1. Hard piping shall be inspected by a certified boiler inspector. Anything over 15 psi. 
1.2. Approvals and final drawings:  
1.2.1. The vendor shall submit to the purchaser, diagrams, bill of materials and specified data on the fluid 
power standards graphics symbols (NFPA(T1)). 
1.2.2. All approval circuits, equipment, etc. shall be submitted to the METALSA Automation engineer 
project representative to be approved. 
1.3. Pressure vessels: 
1.3.1. Pressure vessels shall be constructed with compressed air; it shall work withstand 125 psig 
minimum. 
1.3.2. Pressure vessels shall incorporate pre-set safety relief valves at 170 psig. 
1.3.3. All pneumatic equipment shall be provided with (only) a main airline lockout valve, the pressure 
releases what kind of type needed to shut off the air supply to the equipment.  Each piece of equipment 
shall have a lockable ball valve. 
1.3.4. Machines type long transfer; lockout location should be discussed with the control supervisor 
system. 
1.4. Standard F.R.L. Assembly: 
1.4.1. All connectors for shall be type rotating spigot

1.5.  General requirements: 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of

Page64 
1.5.1. Shall have 24vdc coils only. 
1.5.2. All valves shall have lighted indicators built into coil. 
1.5.3. Pneumatic timers, counters, logic control valves or 2 hand controls are                                         
prohibited. 
1.5.4. Circuits incorporating pneumatic blow-offs for removal of machining chips and dust shall have 
regulated air pressure and each blow-off shall be fitted with an orifice to minimize the consumption of 
air and excess of dust. Pneumatic controlled blow-offs Solenoid shall run only when the machine is 
operating and only be used when other methods of performing are not available. 
1.5.5. Air lines filter shall be installed close to the components being protected (0.005 mm maximum). 
1.5.6. All precision sizing gauges, pneumatic leak test panels, pneumatics logic controls shall have a main 
airline filter element (0.003 mm maximum). 
1.5.7. When a multiple point lubrication system is used it shall be installed in a full compliance with the 
manufacturer’s recommendation to insure an adequate lubrication of all components. 
1.5.8. Lubricators shall be provided (when applies) with quick fill fittings and sight glass. 
1.5.9. Exhaust ports of all pneumatic control, except pilot exhaust, shall be equipped with mufflers and 
located to protect personnel and equipment from exhaust air and blown particles. 
1.5.10. The level of sound and blow-off air shall not exceed 80 db. 
1.5.11. FRL shall be accessible and viewable. 
1.5.12. Filters with automatic drains shall be located a minimum 18” above the floor to allow for collection in 
a 5-gallon bucket or be piped to approved wastewater collection area. 
1.5.13. Filters shall be located on the equipment side of the volume tank to prevent oil from settling out in 
tank. 
1.5.14. Pipe joints shall have a pipe dope sealer.  Pipe dope shall be placed on the male end two full 
threads back from end to minimize pipe dope in system.   
1.5.15. Teflon tape is not acceptable. 
1.5.16. Unions shall be installed at all locations necessary to facilitate maintenance and replacement of 
components. 
1.5.17. Relieving ball valves and safety dump valves shall be mounted so that the exhaust flow is directed 
away from the operator. Maximum height of valves from floor/platform shall be 6’ and 6”. 
1.5.18. Leak test of system shall be pressure tested at normal operating pressure plus 25%. Test pressure 
shall be applied to the closed system for a period of 24 hours with a pressure gauge with a suitable 
range.  No noticeable loss of pressure may be detected to pass test.  Metalsa shall be notified of time 
for the test and reserves the right to monitor and determine pass/fail. 
1.5.19. A Drip leg shall be installed prior to every FRL.  
 
 
1.5.20. Provide drip legs with a downward trap at low points in system.  Ball valves to drain drip legs and 
surge tanks shall be located 18” above the floor to allow for 5-gallon bucket for draining the fluid. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page65 
1.5.21. Filter/regulator/lubricator on compressed air supply as required to protect equipment from 
water/dirt/pressure surges etc. 
1.5.22. All inline devices that have adjustments/maintenance/shut-off valves shall be mounted within 6’ and 
6” of the floor or access platform. 
1.5.23. All connections to main plant header line shall exit top of header pipe to reduce condensation 
problems at equipment. 
1.5.24. Any valve stack with a means of shutting off air supply line (separate from system dump valve) shall 
be equipped with a pressure switch. 
1.5.25. All threads shall be NPT for all tubing and actuators. In SMC components G thread or adapters are 
not allowed. 
1.5.26. For Strongback and Marriage station a proper size air booster shall be consider. 
1.5.27. In case of a piercing station lubrication shall be consider. 
1.5.28. Use of pneumatic adapters is not allowed. 
1.5.29. Plastic Caps shall be considered in all pneumatic connectors. 
 
1.5.30. Oil seal shall be considered in all actuators.  
1.6.  Hoses and fittings 
 
1.6.1. Hoses block valves: Blue (Extended) and Black (Retracted). 
1.6.2. Connection ports: 
A: Extended 
B: Retracted 
1.6.3. Hoses shall be used to bridge equipment flex points. 
1.6.4. Hose bend radius shall not be less than 16 times the inside diameter. 
1.6.5. Hoses shall be installed without any twists and in such a way as to eliminate the possibility of kinking 
and applying bending moments to the fittings. 
1.6.6. Anchor and protect hoses against rubbing and damage from nearby equipment.  
1.6.7. Shall have NPT port connections 
1.6.8. All pneumatic hoses shall get to a distribution block in the base of the fixture to prevent long hoses 
exposed to welding.

2. Safety Pneumatics 
2.1. Safety requirements shall comply with the specifications of the Metalsa “Global safety requirements 
standard” and “Risk Assessment practice” chapters. 
2.2. In case the risk assessment requires a safety component, these good practices shall be used unless the 
risk assessment specifies otherwise. 
2.2.1. Safety/ Lock Out       
2.2.1.1. Every valve shall be LOTO capable: 
 
 
2.2.1.2. Safety dump valves shall be lock-out type. 
2.2.1.3. Lockable Ball valves shall be provided at each manifold valves.  
2.2.1.4. All operator stations shall have an electronic dump valve to exhaust air in that station while light 
curtains or scanners are breached, or gates are open. 
2.2.2. Unintended Movement 
2.2.2.1. In all phases of operation, control systems shall be designed to prevent unintended hazardous 
movement and improper sequencing of actuators, particularly vertical and inclined motions. 
2.2.3.  Pressure regulation 
2.2.3.1. Control shall be provided to maintain the pressure system within the safe limits e.g. where 
pressure regulators are used in pneumatic circuits for safety, they should be of self-relieving 
2.2.3.2. Loss of pressure or pressure drop shall not expose persons to a hazard and should not 
damage the machinery. 
2.2.3.3. The preferred means of protection against excessive pressure in one or more pressure-relief 
valves located to limit the pressure in all related parts in the system. Other means, such as 
pressure regulators, may be used, provided these means satisfy the application requirements. 
2.2.4. Stability 
2.2.4.1. Pressure and flow control valves shall be selected so that changes in actual pressure, actual 
temperature or load do not cause a malfunction or a hazard. 
2.2.5. Tamper resistance 
2.2.5.1. Pressure and flow control valves and their enclosures shall be fitted with tamper-resistant 
devices (e.g. key lock on a pressure regulator) where and unauthorized alteration to pressure or 
flow can cause a hazard or malfunction. 
2.2.6. Safe position 
2.2.6.1. Any actuator required to maintain its position or to adopt a specific position for safety in the 
event of a control system failure shall be controlled by a valve that is held in or switched back to the 
safe position (e.g. spring tension or comparable physical principle). 
2.2.7. Emergency controls 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page69 
2.2.7.1. The system shall incorporate an emergency stop in accordance with ISO 13850,or emergency 
control. 
 
 
 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600

2. SAFETY INTERLOCKS SWITCHES 
2.1. The positively opening switching element directly driven by a cam. The cam and the switching element are 
structurally connected, forming one functional until in the switching process. An actuator (key) operates the 
switch through a positive interlocking switching mechanism at the switching knob. Dual action design is 
preferred for tamper resistance purposes and required for operation. 
 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page87 
 
3. SAFETY GOOD PRACTICES 
3.1. Safety requirements shall comply with the specifications of the Metalsa “Global safety requirements 
standard” and “Risk Assessment practice” chapters. 
3.2. These good practices of this chapter shall be use unless otherwise specified in the risk assessment.  
3.3. DCS shall be use in robotic cell systems to reduce floor space requirements. All floor reductions shall be 
validated at first with Metalsa Automation and Safety specialists. 
3.4. Safety distance calculation shall meet Metalsa Global safety standard requirements meeting ANSI/RIA, 
ISO 13854 and ISO13855 standards. 
3.5. The minimum distance shall be maintained to prevent crushing as stated in ISO 13854 using the Function 
“STOP POSITION PREDICTION” to reduce the space required to the external barrier (Fence, Light curtain, 
scanner, air door, etc.). 
3.6. DCS parameter (Restricted space) should be taught slightly larger than the robots operating space as 
close as is reasonably practicable, always ensuring that the safety distance to the operator meets the 
ISO13855 standard. 
 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page88 
 
3.7. High Speed teach mode (speeds over 250 mm/sec) are not allowed and shall not be implemented and / or 
enabled in any robot.  
3.8. DCS shall be use between welding Robots, Trunnion tables, and handling material robots, to prevent any 
collision among them. 
3.9. All external axis (Trunnion, shuttle, servo lifter, etc.) shall use DCS. 
3.9.1. Trunnion inside robotic station picture reference 
    
 
3.9.2. Trunnion that a person manually loads station picture reference 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page89 
       
 
3.9.3. Any other external axis (Shuttle, servo lifters, etc.) station. 
3.9.3.1. External axis that does not supports DCS functionality shall use Joint speed check. 
4. INTELLIGENT INTERFERENCE CHECK (IIC) 
4.1. To protect the robot, tooling, and TCP. IIC shall be used by the supplier in all welding robotic stations. 
4.2. IIC shall be used only in case of the welding robots.  
4.3. To keep the network as simple and short as possible IIC communication shall be use only among the 
robots of a same station.  
 
 
                                                             Red Zone Shows the Robots using IIC 
 
4.4. In case two or more welding robots of different stations have the risk of colliding. IIC shall be used to 
prevent collisions with welding robots of the same station, and DCS shall be use to prevent collision with 
robots of different stations.  

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA

Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited.

5.3. Each of these sides turns 180° to position the work piece for welding.

5. CATEGORIZE CONDUCTORS 
Refer to the publication for each specific I/O module or block for individual conductor-category 
classification of each I/O line. Segregate all wires and cables into the following three categories: 
Category 
Group conductor cables fitting this 
description 
 
 
Category 1 
Control & ac Power — high-power conductors that are 
more tolerant of electrical noise than category 2 
conductors and may also cause more noise to be 
picked up by adjacent conductors 
• corresponds to IEEE levels 3 (low susceptibility) & 4 
(power). 
 
 
 
Category 2 
Signal & Communication — low-power conductors that 
are less tolerant of electrical noise than category-1 
conductors and should also cause less noise to be 
picked up by adjacent conductors (they connect to 
sensors and actuators relatively close to the I/O 
modules) 
• corresponds to IEEE levels 1 (high susceptibility) & 2 
(medium susceptibility). 
 
Category 3 
Intra-enclosure — interconnect the system 
components within an enclosure  
• corresponds to IEEE levels 1 (high susceptibility) & 2 
(medium susceptibility). 
 
 
 
 
5.1. Route Conductors 
5.1.1. To guard against coupling noise from one conductor to another, when routing wires and cables (both 
inside and outside of an enclosure). Use the spacing given in these general guidelines with the 
following exceptions:  
5.1.2. where connection points (for conductors of different categories) on a device are closer together than 
the specified spacing 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page96 
5.1.3. application-specific configurations for which the spacing is described in a publication for that specific 
application.  
5.1.4. These guidelines are for noise immunity only. Follow all local codes for safety requirements. 
 
Route this category 
of conductor cables: 
According to theseguidelines: 
 
Category 1 
These conductors can be routed in the same cable tray or 
raceway with machine power conductors of up to 600V ac 
(feeding up to 100 hp devices). 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Category 2 
• If it must cross power feed lines, it should do so at right angles.  
• Route at least 5 ft from high-voltage enclosures, or sources of 
rf/microwave radiation. 
 • If the conductor is in a metal wireway or conduit, each segment 
of that wireway or conduit must be bonded to each adjacent 
segment so that it has electrical continuity along its entire length, 
and must be bonded to the enclosure at the entry point.  
• Properly shield (where applicable) and route in a raceway 
separate from category-1 conductors. 
 • If in a contiguous metallic wireway or conduit, route at least 
0.08m (3 in) from category-1 conductors of less than 20A; 0.15m 
(6 in) from ac power lines of 20A or more, but only up to 100 kVA; 
0.3m (1 ft) from ac power lines of greater than 100 kVA. 
 • If not in a contiguous metallic wireway or conduit, route at least 
0.15m (6 in) from category-1 conductors of less than 20A; 0.3m (1 
ft) from ac power lines of 20A or more, but only up to 100 kVA; 
0.6m (2 ft) from ac power lines of greater than 100 kVA. 
 
 
Category 3 
 
Route conductors external to all raceways in the 
enclosure or in a raceway separate from any category-1 
conductors with the same spacing listed for category-2 
conductors, where possible. 
 
Important: These guidelines assume that you follow the surge-suppression guidelines (page 15). 
While these guidelines apply to the majority of installations, certain electrically harsh 
environments may require additional precautions. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page97 
6. ROBOT CONTROLERS 
6.1. The maximum number of stacking controllers is two. All controllers shall be at the edge of the table. 
 
7. ACCESS BOX 
7.1. All safety gates shall have operator safety gate entrance box. 
7.2. For all cell Gates Allen-Bradley or Euchner Access Box shall be considered with key selector. 
7.2.1. The key selector is used to chance the station between “Auto” and in “Teach”. When a request to 
enter is made with the key in Teach the air is still on in the station. Any other way it is needed to drop 
the air from the station with the dump valve. 
    
 
7.2.2. Access Box shall consider with a release handle inside cell. Also, it shall be consider energized to 
unlock.

5. INSTALLATION FACILITIES 
5.1. Terminal Junction Boxes 
5.1.1. Terminal/junction boxes shall be NEMA 12.  Terminal boxes shall be used for inter-connecting unit 
wiring where it will speed up installation as approved by Metalsa.  A minimum of 20% free, or unused 
terminals, shall be provided. No spare wires are to be provided inside cabinets. 
5.1.2. Junction boxes shall be mounted independently of conduits entering them. Brackets, rod hangers, 
bolts or other suitable supporting methods may be used. 
5.1.3. Junction boxes shall be sized as specified, or when not specified shall be sized in accordance with 
NEC requirements. 
5.1.4. All conduit entrances shall be spaced to comply with NEC requirements. Only required openings will 
be allowed and any excess openings will be closed with dust tight covers. 
5.1.5. All junction boxes will be continuous hinged, clamp cover JIC oil tight NEMA 12 Hoffman Engineering 
Corporation. 
5.1.6. All junction boxes shall be furnished with Hoffman removable sub panels. 
5.1.7. All junction boxes shall have a single grounding point. 
5.1.8. Fiberglass reinforced plastic (FRP) boxes shall not be used.  
5.2. Connectors 
5.2.1. In cases where equipment is to be set up and tested on a supplier's floor, disconnected for shipment 
and reconnected at Metalsa's plant, a connector system shall be provided as Metalsa specified. A 
connector system may also be required if the panel is to be connected to existing equipment. 
5.2.2. The control cable and connectors shall contain a minimum of 20% free or unused lines.  All wires 
and connectors should have all wires connected and all spare, wires shall be identified with connector 
and pin number.  All plugs, receptacles and wires will be identified and keyed such that only the proper 
connection can be made. This only applies for multiconductor wires that are connected to a Panel with 
Harting type connectors or cable glands. 
 
5.3.  Brackets and Hangers 
5.3.1. The use of power charged fasteners such as "RAM" or "HILTI" for installing hangers is prohibited. 
Hangers have to be installed with lead anchors, shields, tapcon, or bolts with nuts and lock washers as 
required. All sharp edges on brackets shall be ground smooth to prevent injury. (it is not allowed to use 
rivets on brackets that are supporting something, e.g. plant construction)  
5.4. Power Source and Plant Connections  
5.4.1. All power connections must be marked, balanced, and maintain a power factor of .95 or greater.  
5.4.2. Vendor shall provide all Isolation transformers, step down/up transformers, filters, regulators, or 
suppression equipment.  
5.4.3. Plant power source is:  
5.4.3.1. 480VAC 
5.4.3.2. 3 phases 
5.4.3.3. 60Hz   
5.4.4. Wye/Star grounded 
5.4.5. Contact vendor for minimum interrupting current.  
5.5. Power Distribution 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page117 
5.5.1. All power distribution apparatus shall be mounted true and plumb and unless otherwise specified 
mounting heights from finished floor shall be as follows: 
5.5.2. Convenience and power receptacle to centerline1.06m (3'6") 
5.5.3. Lighting panel boards to top 2.0m (6'6") 
5.5.4. Power distribution panel boards to top 2.14m (7'0") 
5.5.5. For the Power distribution, the supplier shall provide the Power Distribution Panel, and Metalsa shall 
provide the power source for that panel. 
 
 
5.6. Lighting and Control Power  
5.6.1. Shall be on same panels, and there shall be a clear way to differentiate the Control Power breakers 
from the Lighting Power breakers, by labeling correctly every breaker using lamicoids, and one of the 
following: 
5.6.2. Use different color for circuit breakers, one color for Control Power, and another for Lighting Power. 
5.6.3. In the same panel use 2 different sections for each group of breakers, using a clear division between 
both groups. 
5.6.4. Use 2 smaller panels installed together one for Control Power and another for Lighting Power. 
5.7. Lighting and Utility Power  
  
5.7.1. Vendor shall provide lighting on all equipment with overhead obstructions.  
5.7.2. Lighting fixtures shall be 120 volt AC, 4ft or 8ft fluorescent with wire guards. 
5.7.3. Lighting fixtures in assembly areas shall be hung using chain and be connected using six (6) foot 
cords (SO cord is permissible) and twist lock plugs and receptacles mounted overhead. All plugs and 
receptacles shall be of industrial grade. A minimum of 20% spare lighting power and receptacles shall 
be provided.  
5.7.4. At least 2 utility receptacles (120 VAC duplex) shall be installed, piped and wired at every cell. 
Where operators are located there shall be one additional receptacle for each operator in their 
respective area.  
5.7.5. All receptacles shall be individually fused. 
5.7.6. Equipment utility connections to plant services require Metalsa's approval.

1. CONTROL PANELS AND ENCLOSURES 
1.1.1 Templates for all reoccurring control panels types must be provided by Metalsa and followed.  At the 
time of this revision, these types include Standard Panels for Operator Light Screens/Scanners 
(OpBox), Safety Gate Box, HMI Box, HydraulicControl Box, Conveyor Control Box, Main Control Panel, 
and Roll Up Door Box.  These boxes will have associated logic, UDTs and safety logic.  The templates 
for this logic will also be provided and must be followed without deviation. Include templetes, explaining 
the structure of the layout. 
1.1.1.1 Terminal blocks should be Allen Bradley 1492-J or 1492-W style. For the connections of the 
ground wires, there must be a Ground Bar. 
All terminal blocks must be sized 
according to manufacturer’s load specifications 
 
 
1.1.1.2 1492-JD (purple) Double level style may be used for safety circuits only.  Intent for use of this 
style terminal is to keep partner signals of dual chain circuits together.  
1.2  Disconnects 
1.2.1 All motors must have a non-fusible safety switch with auxiliary contact located within fifteen feet of 
the motor.  Contact must be wired back to PLC for monitoring.  This specification may be waived for 
applications using servo-motors. If motor control panel is in line of sight of the motor and within ten feet 
of the motor the motor control panel disconnect will be used as the motor safety switch. 
1.2.2 In welder machines, for the stud cables in addition of the label, there should be a plastic cover 
beneath the label to differentiate the studs (green for Negative stud and Red for positive stud) in both 
sides. 
 
 
1.3 Hydraulic Jet Controls 
1.3.1 Hydraulic jet units shall include an electronic pressure and over-temperature switch.  Switch and 
dump valve position shall be monitored via PLC. 
1.3.2 Tanks shall have a low level warning and low level shut-off switch or suitable replacement.  
1.3.3 Tanks larger than 500 gallons shall have electronic leak detection interlocks. 
1.4 Conductors / Network Cables 
1.4.1 Moving wires must be routed through metallic flex cable trays “Gleason Reel” brand Industrial E-
Type. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page121 
1.4.2 Inside station wires must run through wire trays one inch above floor level and must be LEGRAND 
brand Ladder type, this cable tray must have heavy duty anti-skid plate 1/8” with flanged TRC type 
covers that can withstand walking on them. 
 
 
1.5 Connections 
1.5.1 The use of cable ties within 1m (3 ft.) from a welding application point are prohibited, steel clamps 
and T-Clips shall be used instead when needed. 
2. AUTOMATIC/MANUAL OPERATION 
2.1 Shall be implemented an Auto Memory function in the HMI. This function shall display the last position of 
any actuator in the tooling, in case that another person manually moves an actuator or enters an operation.  
2.2 If an actuator piston loses the right position the sequence shall get stop (robot and tooling). It shall be a 
verification and it will be done with a timer of 500 milliseconds to get sure that it is not a fluctuation of the 
sensor.   
2.2.1 When robot motion is started, the sequence shall stop if the actuator piston miss the right position. 
2.2.2 When robot motion has already started, an error in the part present should not stop the sequence. 
2.3 Required part present should be present prior any actuator or robot movement. If there is not a required 
part present, and alarm should be displayed 
2.4 On the offset option there shall be a routine for every screen in the HMI. When a change made it shall shell 
store changes on the date, users and the offset. It shall record (at least 10) if the offsets in the bracket are 
cleared. 
2.5 Every workstation shall have a routine for sequence that includes all the conditions for the automatic 
operation they shall be divided on steps, and every HMI shall have a banner with the actual step number, 
the sequence status (active/not active) and a description (editable from PLC), the banner shall be present 
on the actuator and a part present screens. (see file “Sequence DSM600.xlsx” on annexes as reference for 
sequence steps). 
2.6 Stack Light 
  
 
 
 
2.6.1 Green (Solid) 
Auto mode selected 
2.6.2 Green (Flashing) 
Manual mode selected 
2.6.3 Red (Flashing)  
Operation Fault 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page122 
3. DRY CYCLE OPERATOR 
3.1 All equipment that have an automatic cycle shall have a Dry Cycle mode of operation, this mode allows the 
operator how run the operation without physical pieces (in automatic mode). This mode is mainly used on 
the improvements for debugging and testing the operation. When the line is running (normal mode) this 
mode has to be fully operational. Consider the Adaptive Welding devices in the operation, even when the 
Dry Cycle works correctly. 
3.2 When the Dry Cycle is working the Safety features cannot be compromised. 
3.3 Sensor Bypass 
3.4 For detection sensors every fixture shall have the Bypass Sensor function, in the HMI. 
3.5 Cannot bypass all the sensors by one fixture, at least one sensor shall be working correctly, and detecting 
the part. 
3.6 For the function of the Bypass Sensor it shall be a password.  
3.7 When a sensor is overstepping the PLC it shall be a register of: user, sensor and date in order to track 
when a sensor is bypassed. The HMI shall indicate that there is an overstep sensor. 
3.8 Offset 
3.8.1 Shall be a screen on the HMI for the applications that have a MH Robot or Fixture Robot that holds a 
bracket during welding, that can control the offset of the bracket on X, Y and Z axes independently of 
the MH Robot.  The offset that applied on the screen shall affect the Welding Robots related to that 
bracket. There shall be a correlation with the Robots programs on the Teach Pendant, in order to apply 
correctly the offset. 
 
3.8.2 There shall be a screen on the Teach Pendant that allows the user to apply offset to a specific Weld 
Bead. The offset shall be capable to adjust in X, Y and Z axes independently. There shall be a 
correlation with the Robots welding programs on the Teach Pendant, in order to apply correctly the 
offset. 
4. ROBOTICS APPLICATIONS 
4.1 Welding Applications 
4.1.1 The equipment of Manufacturer and Welding style depends of Metalsa. 
4.1.2 Welding equipment shall be directly in touch with the robot. 
4.1.3 Ability to control wire feed and gas purge from teach pendant shall be provided 
4.1.4 Nozzle Cleaner, anti-spatter sprayer, wire cutter are controlled by the PLC, they shall be provided for 
the weld robots.  Not more than 4 robots shall share a cleaner. 
4.1.5 Robots shall not be equipped with a quick change welding goose neck style. 
4.1.6 Welding torches shall be only with cooled air. 
4.1.7 Unless otherwise specified by Metalsa, manufacturers wire feeders shall be mounted directly on 
robot. 
4.1.8 Both ends of weld wires shall have a copper, crimp on style connector (Specify type). 
4.1.9 Robots shall not use more than 80% manufacturers specified work envelope. 
4.1.10 Welding power source integration shall include: 
4.1.10.1 TCP/IP port connection from Welder to station Ethernet switch (Stratix). 
4.1.10.2 Fieldbus port connection from Welder to Robot Controller Ethernet Port#2. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited.

5. PRODUCT VERIFICATION 
5.1 Where dedicated Poka Joke / dimensional verification stations are designed into process, station shall 
have the ability to pull off and reload product. 
5.2 Poka Jokes 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page124 
5.2.1 Poka Jokes shall be used for part and feature verifications specified by Metalsa. 
5.2.2 All Poka Jokes shall have a robust design to prevent premature failure due to environment. 
5.2.3 Each cycle shall test Poka Jokes for ability to fail as well as pass condition. 
5.2.4 Metalsa will provide current logic, UDTs and HMI screens for use as a Poka Joke controls template.  
Modifications only be made with Metalsa's consent. 
5.3 Robots welding critical welds shall 
5.3.1 Be equipped with means of automatically determining a weld does not meet weld specifications and 
stopping assembly process or relaying information to repair station. 
5.4  Final Assembly Verification. 
5.4.1 Types 
5.4.1.1 Mechanical hard tooling pin system. 
5.4.1.2 Laser Camera – Perceptron or equivalent style – shall be specified by Metalsa 
5.4.1.3 Station shall be located at the end of assembly process where no other modifications will occur 
to product. (Includes any process that may change alter or effect location of control factors of end 
product). 
6. STAND ALONE STATIONS 
6.1 Control System 
6.1.1 Controllers must be CompactLogix control system. 
6.1.2  Any component shall use 24 VDC. If it is not possible, this case shall be discussed with Metalsa.  
6.1.3 Communication shall be by an Ethernet network.  
6.1.4 Stratix 2000 series industrial switches shall be used.  
6.2 Characteristics Specific machines. 
6.2.1 Welders Projection. 
6.2.1.1 Safety 
6.2.1.1.1 Two Hand Control Relay 
6.2.1.1.1.1 
Must be Pilz PNOZ s6 
6.2.1.1.1.2 
The two hand Relay forces the operator to keep his hands outside the danger zone area 
during the hazardous movement. 
6.2.1.1.2 Two safety relays in series shall cut general energy when any E-Stop condition occurs. 
6.2.1.1.3 Safety relays must follow the ones mentioned in this standard. 
6.2.1.1.4 Shall have one E-Stop in Palm button and main panel. 
6.2.1.1.5 Shall use two hands palm button. 
6.2.1.1.6 E-Stops shall be monitored by the PLC. 
 
6.2.1.1.7 E-Stops shall be connected to PNOZ x8p relay. 
6.2.1.1.8 Electric voltage shall be 24 volts. 
6.2.1.2 Display information. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA

6.2.1.2.1 Four-segment LED display indicator  
6.2.1.2.2 Model:  Banner K80L4GRRR1PQ.

6.2.1.2.4 It is connected to the Compactlogix, this processor sends the 
signals to turn on and turn off the display.

6.2.1.4.1 Displays the nearest cell general information. 
6.2.1.4.2 Communication must be given by Ethernet. 
6.2.1.5 Water flow sensor.

in the fluid, shall be installed a filter with 149 microns on the inlet side of the flow sensor.

7. Field devices 
7.1 Sensing devices shall be weld field immune. 
7.2 Integrator shall include a Banner domed light blue and white at the entrance of the station. In case there is 
another entrance a second Banner domed Valve is needed. 
7.3 Integrator shall include a Banner domed light Red and Green per Operator in manual process stations.  
 
8. Sensors and Cordsets 
8.1 Sensors 
8.1.1 Analog sensors must use IO Link converter 
8.2 Cordsets 
8.2.1 Fix Welding Application; Integrator shall include Turck Aramid Cables 
8.2.2 Movement welding application; integrator shall include Turck cables with silicon protection. 
 
 
8.3  Inductive High Temperature Sensors. 
 
8.3.1 Install this sensor only in applications when the sensors are directly exposed to a high amount of 
weld slag, and high temperatures, and there is no other way to install them. 
 
8.3.2 Refer to the file: “02_Field Devices_PartList”

Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page127 
8.4 Weld Protection. 
When the cables or sensors are exposed to the heat or spark of weld of direct form, must be used any 
of the following options of additional protection. 
8.4.1 Covers sensors  
Refer to the file: “02_Field Devices_PartList” 
8.4.2 Cordsets weld protection. 
Refer to the file: “02_Field Devices_PartList” 
8.4.3 Installation Example.

Material:  
• 
Silicon Protection                    
 
 
•

8.5 Master Blocks, Slave Blocks and Valves 
8.5.1 All Master blocks, slaves, and manifolds shall be in an electrical enclosure to prevent damage: 
8.5.2 Protection enclosures must be used only on the side of the tooling to prevent damage from weld 
spatter 
8.5.3 Approved Part Numbers Refer to the file: “02_Field Devices_PartList” 
8.5.4 Master Blocks shall be used as gateway to IO Link distributed IO, and only one fixture is permitted 
per master block, if a fixture needs more than one master block is permitted and the nomenclature for 
the master blocks shall be MB_Rear_XXX (Station number), MB_Front_XXX (Station number), 
MB_Mid_XXX (Station number), sharing I/O between fixture is not permitted. 
8.5.5 All input sensors hub shall be placed in locations with easy access for maintenance. 
8.5.6 All key enclosures shall have a Key mounted near the box with a chain. 
 
9. Reamer 
9.1 Nozzle clean stations and wired with cordsets (includes connectors molded to the cord at each end) to 
facilitate ease of replacement and be equipped with physical guarding to protect from damage during 
normal operation of equipment. 
10. I/O Link Block. 
10.1 Distributed IO Link Blocks. 
10.1.1 The election of the blocks is according to the application 
10.1.1.1 Teflon in electric arc welding  
10.1.1.2 Aluminium in case of resistance welding  
10.1.2 The plastics are only allowed in operations where weld is not applied. 
10.1.3 All have to have grounded indicated by the manufacturer. 
 
11. HMI GENERAL 
11.1 Specifications 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of

Page129 
11.1.1 All the controllers shall have the option of 2 languages. The first one is English and the second is 
the local language. 
11.1.2 Supplier shall consider the update rate of the PV in one second or higher. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
11.1.3 Input Focus shall be given to the last object created on the display. 
11.1.4 The maximum Tag Update Focus shall be 0.5 seconds. 
11.1.5 The supplier shall use animations only when requires. Any animation shall be approved previously 
by Metalsa.  
11.1.6 The use of images in the PV shall consider the file size during runtime. Remove unused bitmaps. 
JPEGS shall be considering by suppliers in applications. 
11.1.7 Supplier shall consider monochrome Bitmaps of the objects you wish to animate. 
11.1.8 Using Library objects the supplier shall consider basic polygon objects when possible.  
11.1.9 All displays shall be replaced with the exception of Log in Screen, Quality Check, and security 
which are Pop-Ups. 
 
 
11.1.10 In case of closing displays a “Go to” Button shall be use to send to another screen. 
11.1.11 Indexed tag in HMI screens aren´t allowed. 
11.1.12 RFID readers shall be considered on each HMI 
11.1.12.1 Review RFID Reader compatible with Metalsa´s TADI. 
 
11.2 Metalsa Scope 
1.1.1. Metalsa will give the supplier some examples of screens so the supplier can use them. 
1.1.2. SIP Screens will be given to the supplier so the supplier can add them to the station with the marker.  
1.1.3. In case there’s no HMI in a sub-assembly the supplier shall use the HMI closer to the station.

13.13.3 Valves order is placed according to their manifold position. 
13.13.4 In case more than one actuator needs to be activated at the same time, supplier shall consider a 
master button to move both. This button shall be named “Tandem x-x” where “x-x” is the number of 
valves it moves at the same time. For example: “Tandem 1-2-4” moves valves 1, 2, and 4. Supplier 
shall consider that all actuating valves shall be in a predefined position before moving. 
13.13.5 If one screen is not enough for the quantity of valves another screen with the same specification 
can be made. In case there is more than one, two button arrows should be use to go through the 
different screens.

13.13.7 The buttons to activate valves only appears when the run bars are pressed or when it is in manual

14.15 8.15 Weld Check   
 
Use as a countermeasure to avoid missing seam weld. Main cause: 
Not 100% working welding Interface. 
Operators reset procedure after an arc failure or reteach. 
An arc Established signal at the end of each seam weld shall be considered. The robot sends seam number 
to the PLC and the PLC checks if the arc established is ON. 
In case of a missing weld the program shall pop-up the WeldCheck screen, similar to quality check, showing 
the missing seam. To reset the check a login from the user is needed.

his part of the screen appears when you select the robot that you want to monitor when the blue button is 
pressed. At the bottom part of the screen there are the weld seams names, which are marked with a check 
when they’re ok or with a cross mark when the weld seam is wrong. In addition, it shall have the check time 
in seconds of each weld seam.

15. PLC PROGRAMING STRUCTURE 
15.1 PROGRAMING TEMPLATE 
15.1.1 PLC Programming consider Metalsa 24PL project.  
15.2 DISTRIBUTION 
15.2.1 In some cases, a single PLC wouldn’t be enough to include every station in a program. For this 
reason, the supplier shall divide the Line of production in specific areas that will have a common 
program in a PLC that will be in a “System Enclosure” 
 
 
 
15.2.2 The quantity of System Enclosure depends on the size of the Line and Tasks a program will have. 
The supplier shall consider the strategic locations for each System Enclosure. The distribution of the 
System Enclosure shall be approved previously by Metalsa. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page178 
 
 
15.2.3 When multiple stations are referred to a “System Enclosure” each shall break of into Zones. The 
minimum number of zones is one. 
 
 
 
 
15.2.4 A Zone as well as a system Enclosure is breaks into Stations. 
 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page179 
 
 
 
15.2.5 Considering a common limited area of multiple stations. The routines or safeties should be 
considered in the “Zone_Enclosure” Task. 
 
 
15.3 MAIN TASKS 
15.3.1 System Enclosure 
 
 
15.3.2 This Task has the common routines of a zone or a group of zones.  
15.3.3 The minimum quantity of zones inside a system enclosure is one.  

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page180 
15.3.4 In case there is more than one System_Enclosure in a process; the name of the System_Enclosure 
should be number according to the flow of material. For example: “System_Enclosure_1”.  
15.3.5 The numbers shall start from number 1. Nevertheless, the supplier shall propose the numbering 
method, quantity, and naming of each System_Enclosure. 
15.3.6 A program can only have one System_Enclosure Task. Correspondingly, the name of this task shall 
be unique in the same process. 
15.3.7 Routines inside a System Enclosure.

15.3.9 Use to Jump to the other subroutines.

15.4 SPECIAL TASKS 
1.2.9. Each Special Task shall be import to the PLC that has the routine of the marking station. 
1.2.10. The tasks that shall be imported are: 
1.2.10.1. SIP_Transaction 
1.2.10.2. DataBase_TXN_Failure_Cat 
1.2.10.3. DataBase_TXN_Machine_Cat 
1.2.10.4. DataBase_TXN_KeepAlive 
1.2.10.5. DataBase_TXN_Downtime 
1.2.10.6. DataBase_TXN_Part_Program 
1.2.10.7. DataBase_TXN_Station_Report 
1.2.10.8. Program_Control_Station 
1.2.11. Metalsa will provide the supplier Three ID numbers that will serve as reference for each station.  
1.2.12. Each ID will be mention as “Corporate ID”, “Address ID” and “Misc ID”.  
1.2.13.  Address ID is use only in stamping process. 
1.2.14. Each ID shall be Unique.  
1.2.15. The name of the “Station” and “Zone” is repeated among the different tasks. The supplier shall 
change the name corresponding to the station or zone name provide by Metalsa. 
1.2.16. Find and Replace can be used to help/facilitate this activity. Is strongly recommended that the 
name of the station should be replaced before importing.  
1.2.17. The place in which the station name should be inserted/change is mark as follows: “Station”. 
1.2.18. The place in which the Zone name should be inserted/change is mark as follows: “Zone”. 
1.2.19. In case the name is “OP840” the name of the variable should be: 
“Program_Control_OP840.Paro_CntrlDepartamento”, instead of 
“Program_Control_Station.Paro_CntrlDepartamento” 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page192 
 
15.4.1 In the task “DataBase_TXN_Downtime” in the routine “Downtime_Register_Station” it should be 
replace the “Station” with the name of the station.  
15.4.2 In the Rung one, in the Routine Previously mentioned, the “Corporate ID” shall be insert as a value 
of the “Program_Control_OP840.ID”. 
 
15.4.3  In the Rung five, in the routine previously mentioned, the “Misc ID” shall be inserted as a value of 
the “Station_SIP.MFG.CYC_TIME”. 
 
15.4.4  “In Program_Control_Station”, in the Routine IO, in rung 1 the value of 
“Station_Model_Type.Model_From_Prev_Station” shall be replaced with the Variable that verifies the 
current model selected.  
15.4.5  “In Programa_Control_Station”, in the Routine IO, in rung 4 the signal of cycle end shall be placed. 
15.4.6 “In Programa_Control_Station”, in the Routine IO, in rung 4 the value of the “preset” shall be the 
size of the batch of pieces predetermined by Metalsa.

17. SERVICES 
17.1 WATER 
17.1.1 Cooling System 
 
Refer to “09_Services_PartList” document for approved components for the installation of cooling 
system. 
NOTE:  It shall make a pressure strength (2 Kg/cm2) leak test for 24 hours with air. 
 
Recommendations: 
• To consider gosse neck in the exit not to lose the liquid of the system. 
• To consider intake common of ¾ until it should be needed additional by requirements of 
equipment. 
• The water hardness shall be indicated in percentage of salts. 
17.2 MIX GAS 
Refer to “09_Services_PartList” document for approved components for the installation of mix gas. 
17.2.1 For Gas supplier shall consider Black Pipe. 
17.2.2 A mass Flow Transmitter shall be use in the main supply for the Main Distribution Ring. This Mass 
Flow.  
17.2.2.1 The flow meter shall consider 1.5” Ansi 150lbs for Argon and CO2. 
17.2.2.2 The flange shall be stainless steel for 316L  
17.2.2.3 The communication shall be ethernet. In case is not possible a Modbus RS484 with USB port 
and ethernet to configure shall be include with a R-232/422/485 Modbus TCP to serial 
communication Gateway 
Recommendations: 
• To run test of waterproof 4 or 6 hours. 
17.3 DISTRIBUTION 
17.3.1 Plant drops supply by Metalsa will be at most 2’’ for air and 1.5” for gas. Integrator shall consider 
this information for air and gas calculations. 
17.3.2 Supplier shall add a tooling ring or Bus type distribution for air and gas per zone. Size of zone shall 
not be greater than 7 stations unless specify otherwise by Metalsa.

in multiple zones. 
17.4.1.3 The drop from suppliers shall be consider at the end of a zone, in the first or last station to 
control the solenoid from the closest Master Block from the station provide by supplier.

19. SAFETY ASSEMBLY PRACTICES 
19.1 Safety requirements shall comply with the specifications of the Metalsa “Global safety requirements 
standard” and “Risk Assessment practice” chapters. 
19.2 These good practices of this chapter shall be use unless otherwise specified in the risk assessment.  
19.3 Pedestals projection and Spot welding (manual process) 
19.3.1 Machines need to be provided with a guard for spatter protection. (Point 1 in picture) 
19.3.2 Jig to allocate the parts and keep hand of the worker out of the pitch points. (Point 2 in picture) 
19.3.3 Fumes extraction if the building is not capable to extract all the fumes. (Point 3 in picture) 
19.3.4 Manual feeding is allowed but Safety department shall approve the process before going forward 
with the construction of it. (Point 4 in picture) 
19.3.5 Documented process for electrodes cleaning explaining how to avoid pitch points. 
19.3.6 Documented process for flatness testing. 
19.3.7 Documented process for electrodes changes. 
19.3.8 Documented process for destructive test.

the owner is prohibited.

19.4 Riveting and Manual Spot Welding 
19.4.1 Place 2 action buttons presence and ensure that the position of the buttons do not get caught near 
point in the operator's hands. 
19.4.2 Install security steel cable to the trolley and rail according to the weight of the same. 
19.4.3 It should not be the source of power above the operator. 
19.4.4 Having an area when not being in use (base hook) to prevent stroke with operator

1. General 
1.1. Codes and Regulations 
1.1.1. Provide electrical equipment to meet the applicable requirements of the following guidelines:                          
• 
NFPA 33 – (Standard For Spray Application Using Flammable Or Combustible Materials) 
• 
NFPA 70 – (National Electrical Code) 
• 
NFPA 77 – (Recommended Practice On Static Electricity) 
• 
NFPA 86 – (Standard for Ovens and Furnaces) 
• 
NFPA 54 – (National Fuel Gas Code Handbook) 
1.2. Control Panels and Enclosures 
1.2.1. Enclosures 
1.2.1.1. Enclosures that have exposure to dripping water or corrosive liquids shall be NEMA4X. 
1.2.1.2. If supplier propose any additional NEMA type of enclosure shall need METALSA approval.  
2. Safety good practices 
2.1. Safety requirements shall comply with the specifications of the Metalsa “Global safety requirements 
standard” and “Risk Assessment practice” chapters. 
3. Field devices 
3.1. Sensing Devices 
3.1.1. For long distance position sensing/tracking, Pepperl+Fuchs WCS2 Code Rail Readers shall be used. 
(with Ethernet/IP comms adapter).  
 
NOTE: If supplier propose any additional NEMA type of enclosure shall need METALSA approval.  
3.1.2. High heat resistant sensors shall be use whenever the applications gets close to a high temperature 
zone. 
3.1.3. Considerar hermeticidad/humedad para temas de limpieza-mantenimiento con agua a presión 
3.1.4. Hydraulic systems shall not be use or must be certified whenever it is close to the Combustion 
systems (E.g. Cure oven) to prevent any safety hazard 
3.1.5. Sensors for tracking must be protected against splatter or contact with liquids. 
4. Process Tanks 
4.1. Washers/Cleaners/ conditioner/phosphate/sealer/rinse/permeates 
4.1.1. If the pipe is steel, you can choose to use contactors require Metalsa´s Consent.  

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page224 
4.1.2. If the pipe is CPVC, the use of a soft starter is recommended to avoid damage to the pipe. 
4.1.3. The usage of Contactor in Pumps shall require Metalsa´s Consent. 
4.1.4. For tilt motion a VFD shall be used. 
4.1.5. All tank pumps shall have a flow sensor with PLC connection. Please refer to part list for 
specification. 
4.1.6. shall have a monitor level sensor placed on the weir of the tank. with PLC connection. Please refer to 
part list for specification. 
4.1.7. At least 1 tank of each type must have a bypass solenoid valve for refilling/level recover in automatic 
mode/ production 
4.1.8. The tanks of: cleaner, conditioner, sealer, E-coat, and permeate must have a pH sensor. 
4.1.8.1. The tanks of: rinses, E-coat and permeate must have a conductivity sensor. 
4.1.8.2. Conductivity sensor shall control water addition 
4.1.8.3. PLC shall have indicators/alarms when process parameters are about to get out of range. 
(define at what range the alarm would work). 
4.1.8.4. All pumps above 30HP must have VFD 
4.1.8.5. Pumps must be Gusher 
4.1.9. The cleaner and phospate tanks must have a temperature sensor to measure the water of the tank 
4.1.10. If low level in the tank is detected, the system shall activate the Solenoid valve to recover the level 
required.  
4.1.11. Phospate tank pneumatic line connected to the sludge suction pipe at the bottom of the tank  
4.1.12. Purge system/ sludge pipe cleaning 
4.2. Ecoat tank 
4.2.1. VFD shall be used in pumps.  
4.2.2. Supplier should provide a removable and interchangeable protector shell to avoid paint going though 
anode cells wires and outside the e-coat tanks. Protector shell design must be approved by Metalsa. 
Rubber/plastic material is not allowed. 
4.2.3. An individual Line reactor shall be installed at the input of every VFD in ECOAT Control Enclosure. 
4.2.4. Special tank covering-- Tlaloc 
4.2.5. Shall have a flow sensor with PLC connection. Please refer to part list for specification. 
4.2.6. Shall have a monitor level sensor placed on the weir of the tank. with PLC connection. Please refer 
to part list for specification. 
4.2.7. Shall have temp sensor with PLC connection. 
4.2.8. Guard with Interlock to limit access 
5. Tanks External Equipment 
5.1. Oberlin 
5.1.1. Oberlin feed pump shall be hydropneumatic. Please refer to part list for specification. 
5.1.2. Feedback o comm con PLC de la línea. (señales como inicio, stop, alarmas). 
Note: Please refer to Process Monitoring (i4.0) section for specific sensor per process stage. 
5.2. Boiler 
5.2.1. Boiler must be RITE brand. 
 
5.2.2. Need to have one back up boiler. 
5.2.3. There should be connections installed for cleaning. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page225 
5.2.4. Must have a pressure sensor installed in the water inlet of each boiler. 
5.2.5. Hot and Cold water loops must be insulated with a minimum 1” fiberglass insulation and backed up 
with additional pump. 
5.2.6. Flame controls relays must be Honeywell (for boilers and burners).  
5.2.7. Boiler selection must be included in the PLC. 
5.2.8. There should be alarms in the PLC of boiler failures. 
5.2.9. Gas train must have a gas flow meter installed. (Gas consumption monitoring). 
 
5.3. Anolyte Tank 
5.3.1. Shall have a flow sensor for the output of the pump with PLC connection. Please refer to part list for 
specification. 
5.3.2.  Shall have a flow sensor per each anodic cell with PLC connection.  
5.3.3. Shall have a monitor level sensor placed on the weir of the tank. with PLC connection. Please refer 
to part list for specification. 
5.3.4. Must have PH and conductivity sensor 
5.3.5. Temperature sensor**** 
5.4. Heat exchanger 
Flow sensor.  
Paint exchanger in and out temperature sensor  
 
5.5. Ultrafilters 
5.5.1. Flow meter on the entrance of ultrafilters. 
 
5.6. Rectifiers 
5.6.1. Rectifiers Enclosure shall be mounted in a controlled environment. (extraction de calor y un area 
considerable por la generación de calor) 
5.6.2. Rectifier’s system shall have their own PLC. Please refer to General Control Std part list 
5.6.3. Rectifier’s system shall be prepared for an external start and stop signal. These signals shall be 
programmed using consumed-produced with the PLC of the line. 
5.6.4. **6Consultar con controlled power de la distancia optima entre el rectificador  
5.6.5. Connection board/ power connection to the cell at the foot of the paint tank with free access. (copper 
bar) 
5.6.6. Current measurement per cell 
5.6.7. For the ground follow the manufacturer´s recommendations. 
5.6.8. The ground must be sheltered (aboid risk of paint splatter) 
5.7. Storage tank  
5.7.1. Lamp system feedback UV (OK – no OK) – add part number of lamp and bomb 
5.7.2. Flow sensor for water bomb DI/DO 
5.7.3.  Level sensor.  
5.7.4. Full automation of transfer system from process tank to storage tank  
5.7.5. Provide level sensors for each holding tank and need to be connected to the main line control 
(Interlock for turn on/off the transfer pumps). 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of

Page226 
5.7.6. Level sensor. Float ball sensors are not allowed. 
5.7.7. Three-way valves (check) 
6. Cure oven 
6.1. Shall be thermocouples or any other temperature measuring device in the entrance, exit and center of the 
oven. 
6.2. Temperature will be controlled by PLC with adjustment and display (+/- 5° F). 
6.3. A Flame controller shall be used to control the burner. (It is not allowed to used a PLC to control the 
burner). 
6.4. Combustion systems (E.g. Cure oven) shall have a gas detection system to prevent any safety hazard. 
6.5. Dynamic self-check ultraviolet flame detector shall be used to detect flame in the burner. 
 
 
6.6. Flor meter and gas consumption totalizer at the inlet 
6.7. The thermocouple gain can be modified by the user 
6.8. Temperature monitoring in the combustion chamber for prevention  
6.9. Curing box temperature monitoring  
6.10. Curing oven must have indirect heat, also the flame don´t be in direct contact with the paint 
6.11. Necessary feedback signals from the burner flame control system to the PLC 
• 
Air flow 
• 
P.S High of gas 
• 
P.S Low of gas 
• 
Burner on 
• 
Temperature 
6.12. Motors used near the oven must have specifications to work in high temperature.  Type H (180 c) N(200 
c) S (240 c) 
7. Conveyor System 
7.1. Motor Starters and Contactors in Applications other than Motor Control Centers 
7.1.1. The conveyor shall have forward and reverse capability. 
7.1.2. Motor Starters shall only be used in place of VFD with Metalsa’s consent. 
7.2. Shall be limit switches to detect pallet type 
7.3. Cabinet must be protected from splashes and carryovers 
7.4. Shall stop in case of overload. 
7.5. Shall be able to acknowledge positions along its length. 
7.6. An automatic lubrication system shall be included for all chains in the system. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page227 
7.7. For those chains that are exposed to carry over, a cleaning system shall be included that prevent rust in 
chains. 
8. Lifting system 
8.1. Hoist 
8.1.1. Overtravel and position sensing – barcode. Optical readers not allowed. 
8.1.2. Should have manual mode 
8.1.3. Drives shall not be above 75% of capacity 
8.1.4. VFD’s for transfer system (hoists) 
8.1.5. I/O link with ethernet must be the communication system  
8.1.6. Shall have visual aids to identify the current state of the hoist (e.g. changing color led band) 
8.1.7. Hoist recipe modification or new hoist programs must be easy to implement to increase process 
flexibility and reduce implementation time in future frame programs. 
8.1.8. Wireless communication from Hoists to PLC via ethernet. Capability to add additional ethernet ports 
on hoists communication system. 
8.1.9. PLC failure alarm list must be specific and the possibility of adding latter on production more failures 
modes without requiring a change on hoist programing must be included

1. PURPOSE 
1.1. This document has been issued by Metalsa, to provide environmental health and safety global standards 
as a requirement to build, design, fabricate or modify any equipment, tool or any elements used in the 
manufacturing process in order to comply with EHS standards and to guarantee the integrity of the 
personnel within our operations. This document is in addition to other requirements defined by the EHS 
global team as part of continuous improvements. 
1.2. Attention!  
1.2.1. It is the responsibility of the value proposition area to ensure that they are in possession of the latest 
revision of this quotation guideline prior to quoting or working on any job.
