3. Responsibilities 
3.1. All Metalsa departments are required to comply with the below standards. 
3.2. Any decision to deviate from these standards require the approval of the strategy business unit coordinator 
and the EHSS central coordinator.  This decision must be based on an approved risk assessment 
methodology. 
3.3. Any final decision to deviate from standard will be based only on current safety standards to ensure 
compliance. If modifications are required to the standards to mitigate a risk, such modification must comply 
with local, state and federal regulation(s) and standards, and current, applicable consensus safety 
standards. 
3.4. A risk assessment is required to be completed by the supplier and/or manufacturer for all new machines, 
equipment, tools and other elements used in Metalsa manufacturing process.  Including risk of products, 
processes, materials and environment. 
3.5. Tools that are being controlled by another machine/equipment does not require a risk assessment (such 
as toolings in press, toolings in assembly universal cells), this because the safety in the tooling shall be 
meet by the machine / equipment. 
3.6. The risk assessment, if done by a third party other than the supplier or manufacturer, must be agreed 
upon by both the supplier/manufacturer and Metalsa. 
3.7. Risk assessment requirements: 
3.7.1. Must be able to identify all tasks perform in that operation. 
3.7.2. Must be able to identify all potential hazards. 
3.7.3. Must quantify risk presented by the hazards. 
3.7.4. Must be able to demonstrate that the risk has been reduced as low as reasonably practicable 
(ALARP), in accordance with current international electrotechnical commission (IEC) standard 61511), 
and to a level acceptable to Metalsa. 
3.7.5. Must use umbrella iso and/or ANSI standards setting forth requirements on risk reduction; and 
3.7.6. Must use life cycle and safety integrity level (SIL). As describe in the following diagram. 
3.7.6.1. 
 
3.8. Third party validation is required for any equipment, process, tools, or elements used in the manufacturing 
process to ensure compliance with current and applicable standards for each country and region. 

 
 
 
 
Copyright © METALSA 
Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca, Nuevo Leon, México, C.P. 66600 
Reproduction in whole or in part, without the previous and express written consent of  
the owner is prohibited. 
Page233 
3.9. Risk assessment and validation must be completed by a TUV 2 Rheinland certified professional, or 
another professional possessing equivalent and similar education. Including training, experience, 
qualifications and /or license(s) approved by Metalsa. Is required to follows the functional safety life cycle 
methodologies, practices, and processes to ensure safety standards and principles are applied and 
properly implemented based on the agreed upon risk assessment process and safety system functional 
requirements. 
3.9.1. When it is impractical or infeasible for a TUV 2 Rhienland certified professional to perform the risk 
assessment and validation, another professional possessing equivalent or substantially similar 
education, training, experience, qualifications, and/or license(s) can be used, but shall require the 
approval of the EHSS central coordinator. 
3.10. Regulations vary between each country, operations, and facilities.  Accordingly, each manufacturer 
and/or supplier is responsible to ensure compliance with all country, territory, federal, state, and local laws 
applicable to the location for which each process, equipment, etc., will be shipped, setup and utilized. 
3.11. Full documentation is required regarding risk assessments, risk assessments validation, control 
validation, lockout and tagout maps, operation manuals, and other documents required in plant readiness 
and a09. (reference document: plant readiness, a09, job safety analysis, safe handling materials, etc.). Full 
documentation is required to be provided to the EHS central coordinator, EHS plant coordinator, and value 
proposition team member responsible for ensuring the above outlined process is followed. 
3.12. All documents must be marked “confidential” as these may contain proprietary information related to 
Metalsa processes. These documents are not to be shared with any other parties without the written 
approval of the legal representative of Metalsa.  
3.13. Hardcopies of this file are uncontrolled. Controlled Documents reside electronically on the MOS portal. 
3.13.1. For link to controlled document contact Automation Operations Advance Manufacturing (OAM). 
3.13.2. Individuals using an uncontrolled copy are responsible for ensuring that they are using the latest 
revision of this document.  
4. Standards 
4.1. Manufacturers, suppliers, vendors or other entities affected by this global Metalsa standard for safety 
requirements shall ensure equipment, processes and other materials built for and/or provided to Metalsa 
comply with the applicable requirements  set forth in the following, non-exhaustive list of regulatory and 
consensus standards. The following  regulatory and consensus standards are those that may reasonably 
be encountered with Metalsa processes and operations, but do not necessarily represent every standard, 
regulation or other law that may apply in a given situation. Thus, it is the obligation of any and all 
manufacturers, suppliers, vendors, etc., to research and identify all additional, relevant consensus 
standards, regulations and other legal requirements that may pertain to the equipment, process or 
materials being produced and/or provided to Metalsa, and then consult with the appropriate Metalsa 
representative  on such. All applicable standards are to be consulted, followed and strictly adhered to in 
their entirety. 
4.2.  if a deviation to any component or provision of a standard or regulation cannot be met, either in part or in 
whole, the deviation must be approved of by the EHSS central coordinator and the EHSS plant 
coordinators respectively. 
4.3. Manufacturers, suppliers, vendors or other entities affected by this global Metalsa standard for safety 
requirements shall follow the most current version of any consensus or regulatory standard.  In the event a 
new version of any applicable consensus standard will become effective after the date the manufacturer, 
vendor, supplier, etc., is contracted or commissioned for a particular project, they shall ensure that all 
equipment, materials, processes, etc., is compliant with the most current version of such upon delivery.

5. PREREQUISITES  
5.1. Any Metalsa employee assigned to design, fabricate, modify, install or validate environmental health and 
safety equipment should be trained and access to below documents 
5.1.1. Standards summary list (section 2 / previous section). 
5.1.2. Mos safety manuals 
5.1.3. Metalsa global safety standards guidelines and best practices 
5.1.4. Contractor environmental, health and safety program 
6. Validation 
6.1. Once equipment is installed at the integrator facility, (manufacturer, supplier, vendor, etc).  A complete 
validation of safety devices must be performed by the integrator, based on risk assessment performed 
consistent with the requirements established by this Metalsa standard. Validation must be conducted by 
trained/experienced controls engineer(s) who has working knowledge of standards referenced in this 
Metalsa standard/document.  
6.2. Once the equipment is installed at Metalsa’s facility(ies), an additional third party validation is required. In 
the event any deviation is detected, the deviation must be corrected before starting the operation of the 
equipment. Any exception to this requirement must be escalated by the project leader and approved in 
writing by the plant coordinator and/or strategic business coordinator, 
6.3. After completed operation installation at the final location, it is required to use Metalsa task risk 
assessment to ensure all hazards involved in the operation are mitigated or eliminated. Any remaining, low 
risk hazard(s) shall be included in the applicable job safety analysis(es) to provide training and hazard 
recognition to employees. 
6.4. If, during job safety analysis process, an additional hazards are identified, the above risk assessment 
process must be completed to determine appropriate methods of control following all current safety 
standards and/or regulations.

INTENT 
This standard has been written by Metalsa, for the purpose of providing a guideline for color 
specifications. These specifications have to be used in addition to, instead of manufacturer’s 
recommendations and ratings. 
 
It is required for the quotation of assembly process to guarantee the safety of our workers, the 
quality of our products and the capital invested, as well as offer to our customers a flexible, 
innovative, and integral competitive assembly process which put our proposals above the 
competition. 
 
ATTENTION! 
It is responsibility of the vp(t1) area to ensure that they are in possession of the latest revision of 
this quotation guideline prior quoting or working on any job. Our standards will be made 
available to our suppliers by authorized personal from purchasing area. 
 
 
 
SCOPE 
This guideline is effective for all new process quoted (value proposition area), current process 
engineering changes & capacity up adaptation (product management), improvements (process 
engineering & operations). 
 
 
 
RESPONSABILITIES 
1. Metalsa as a global company must comply with this guideline for the scope already 
explained above. 
 
2. This guideline offers minimum process requirements to comply, if not, there must be a 
justification approved from the plant manager of the location and the area coordinator 
from the area who is not according to this guideline. 
 
3. If any location finds any better practice than the ones presented here, the department must 
notify to knowledge center kc in order to determine if the guide must suffer any 
modification. 
 
4. Because of the different regulation on each country, every area is responsible to comply 
with the federal and local laws on each process at your location.

Purpose 
Support and guide the engineering team together with the project team in the design of 
welding cells and other workstations (manual welding and rework) through clear 
guidelines that indicate the lighting needs to be met according to the work. 
 
Introduction 
In this document determines the optimum lighting requirements for normal operation and 
emergencies. It is important to determine and provide clear guidelines regarding lighting 
levels as this affects the performance of operators and is a determining factor for the 
design of safe and ergonomic work environments. 
This standard is based entirely on the Mexican Official Standard NOM-025-STPS-2008 
Lighting conditions in workplaces. 
In addition, a link is attached containing the requirements regarding the lighting levels 
applicable in Argentina, as they differ from those applicable in the United States and 
Mexico. 
Objective 
The following guidelines must be used to evaluate and determine the optimal lighting 
levels of each workstation for the safety and performance of the operators. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent.

When assessing the lighting conditions, follow the indications in Table 1 and Table 3  
(Maximum allowable levels of reflection factor). The following points must be also 
considered: 
a) Distribution of work areas, lighting system (number and distribution of 
luminaires), machinery and work equipment. 
b) Lamp wattage. 
c) Description of the illuminated area: colors and type of surfaces of the premises 
or building. 
d) Description of the visual tasks and work areas, in accordance with the previous 
table 
e) Description of the workstations that require localized lighting 
f) Information on the worker's perception of lighting conditions to the employer. 
 
In Mexico and USA 300 lux is considered as the standard level for assembly (Cells) and 
projection welding stations. 1000 lux is considered as the standard level for 
inspection and repair areas. 
In the case of Argentina it will be necessary to review the applicable standards in force, 
please consider the following illumination levels (Table 2) obtained from the Argentina 
Official Standard Argentine Official Standard IRAM-AADL J 20-06. (Click to visit). 
Table 2 
Visual Job Task 
Work Area 
Illumination Levels 
Lux 
Moderately critical and prolonged tasks, with 
medium details. 
Medium-sized, mechanical, and manual 
work, inspection and assembly; ordinary 
office work such as reading, writing and 
archiving. 
300-750 
Severe, prolonged and low-contrast tasks 
Fine work, mechanical and manual work, 
assembly, and inspection; extra-fine paint, 
blowing, sewing dark clothes. 
750-1500 
 
 
For assembly cells and projection welding stations and for local lighting of the 
rework or recovery areas use LED lighting fixtures. Luminaires installed within one 
meter or less of the operator's view require a diffused or textured acrylic cover to avoid 
visual glare. 
 
 
 
 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
2. Control & Maintenance 
2.1 
Control 
If the result of the measurement shows that the lighting levels in the work areas or visual 
tasks are below the levels indicated in Table 1 or that the reflection factors are above 
those established in Table 3 , the necessary control measures must be adopted, including 
maintenance of the luminaires, modification of the lighting system or its distribution and/or 
installation of supplementary or localized lighting. For the latter control measure, where 
greater illumination is required, the following aspects should be considered: 
a) Avoid direct or reflection glare to the worker. 
b) Select a visual background suitable for the worker's activities. 
c) Avoid blocking the lighting during the performance of the activity, and 
d) Avoid areas with sudden changes in lighting. 
Once the control measures have been carried out, an evaluation must be made to verify 
that the new lighting conditions comply with the provisions of this Standard. 
 
2.1.1 Location of measurement points. 
The measurement points must be selected according to the needs and characteristics of 
each work center, in such a way that they describe the lighting environment in a reliable 
way, considering: the production process, the classification of the areas and work 
stations, the required lighting level in the following table, the location of the luminaires 
with respect to the work planes, the calculation of the area index corresponding to each 
of the areas, the position of the machinery and equipment, as well as the risks reported 
to the workers. 
 
2.1.2 Reflection factor 
To determine the reflection factor on the work plane and walls that, due to their proximity 
to the worker, affect the lighting conditions, the following methodology must be followed. 
 
a) A first measurement (𝐸1) is made with the luxmeter photocell facing the surface, at a 
distance of 10 cm ± 2 cm, until the reading remains constant. 
 
b) The second measurement (𝐸2), is made with the photocell facing the opposite 
direction and resting on the surface, to measure the incident light. 
 
c) The surface reflection factor (𝐾𝑓) is determined with the following equation 
 
𝐾𝑓= 𝐸1
𝐸2
 (100) 
 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
 
Once the result has been obtained, the maximum permissible levels of the reflection 
factor must be compared with the following table. 
 
Table 3. Maximum Allowable Levels of Reflection Factor.  
 
Concept 
Maximum Permissible Reflection Levels (𝑲𝒇) 
Walls 
60% 
Work Plate 
50% 
 
Note: Glare is considered to exist in the work area and workstation when the reflection 
value (𝐾𝑓) exceeds the values established. 
 
 
2.2 
Maintenance 
The following should be considered in the maintenance of the luminaires: 
a) The cleaning of the luminaires. 
b) Ventilation of the luminaires. 
c) The replacement of luminaires when they cease to operate, blinks and/or lose their 
luminosity. 
d) The elements that prevent direct and reflected glare, as well as the flicker effect 
 
 
3. Audit  
The following specifications and documentation are mandatory for subsequent audits: 
1. An initial survey of the workstations should be carried out containing the following 
information: 
a) The descriptive report of the normal operating conditions under which the 
evaluation of lighting levels was performed, including descriptions of the process, 
facilities, workstations, and the number of workers exposed per area and 
workstation. 
 
b) The distribution of the evaluated area, indicating the location of the measurement 
points. 
 
c) The results of the evaluation of the illumination levels indicating their uncertainty. 
 
d) Comparison and interpretation of the results obtained, against those established in 
Table 1 and Table 3. 
 
e) The time at which the measurements were taken. 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
 
f) The maintenance program. 
 
g) The copy of the document that supports the calibration of the luxmeter issued by an 
accredited and approved laboratory in accordance with the provisions of the Federal 
Law on Metrology and Standardization, and that complies with the provisions 
stipulated in this Standard. 
 
h) The technical conclusion of the study.  
 
i) The control measures to be developed and the implementation program. 
 
j) Name and signature of the person responsible for the study. 
 
k) Evaluation results up to compliance with Table 1 and Table 3. 
 
Every two years an evaluation must be performed to verify that the lighting conditions 
are maintained according to the standard. 
2. Carry out the control of the illumination levels, as established in subtopic 2.1. Control. 
 
3. Inform all workers about the risks that may be caused by glare or a deficient level of 
lighting in their work areas or workstations. 
 
4. Perform annual visual acuity, campimetry and color perception tests for workers who 
work in areas of the workplace with special lighting. color perception to workers who 
carry out their activities in areas of the work center with special lighting. 
 
5. Develop and implement a maintenance program for workplace lighting fixtures, 
including emergency lighting systems, as established in the maintenance section. 
 
6. Install emergency electric lighting systems in those areas of the work center where the 
interruption of the artificial light source represents a risk in the visual task of the 
workstation. 
 
 
 
 
 
 

 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
4. Appendix A 
Lighting Calculations  
The calculation by the zonal cavity method is recommended, considering the assembly 
height of 7-8 meters, the work plane at 1 meter and reflectance according to the type of 
work, assembly has a heavy industrial environment (0-30-10). 
 For the calculation, the people in charge of the engineering can use a free online software 
called Visual3D to determine the required number of luminaires using the “. ies" format 
obtained from the luminaire manufacturer.

12 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
1 General Information 
a. Objective  
Having the standard of manufacture frame assembly lines with which suppliers have a 
better view of what we expect to receive from their services. 
b.  Manufacturing 
The tooling design must be delivered to start manufacturing Supplier / Metalsa 
feedback if there are doubts designs. (Parts, materials, thermal treatment, structure). 
c. Design 
The supplier is responsible for guaranteeing that all internal and external designs sub 
contracted are handle to Metalsa’s standard manufacturing concepts design. 
d. Engineering 
The supplier is responsible for providing documentation to final manufacturing level, 
including the modifications made 3 month later of start of production 
e. Technical information 
New equipment training and technical information of maintenance, functionality, and 
critical points. (see appendix A) 
f. Documentation provided by supplier 
The supplier shall provide the information as its indicated in Appendix B. 
All dimensions for mechanical systems shall be in metric unless otherwise agreed 
upon. 
g.  Reference points according to the GDT 
In the manufacturing of registers supports we must take into account reference points 
that marks the GD&T.  
All reference point should go bolting and doweled (ex. PLPs, part registers, holding 
pilots). 
Must comply as far as possible the size of the reference area indicated in the GD&T’s 
part, in case of reference holes be aware about its tolerances for the manufacture of the 
locating pins see Appendix C 
h. Screws 
The type of fasteners must be metric socket screw and lock washer, and of the same 
size, unless otherwise specified, whenever possible.  This will reduce the number of tools 
required for service. Also follow the guidelines indicated in Appendix D 
i. Dowel 
The type of dowel used must have extraction thread and air exit plane. 
Should also cover the extraction thread with hex head screw. 
The drilled must be all thru whenever possible 
 
 
 
 
 

 
13 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
j. Lubrication  
All moving parts must have lubrication system. And when the lubrication system is 
inaccessible, we must centralize this point using a duct network following the guidelines. 
(indicated on Appendix E) 
k. Materials and thermal treatment 
Specified in each of the parts according to their work and performance. 
l. Certification of finished table 
Must be at 100% with the supplier and at 20% in the production installation 
m. Bushing 
It is recommended that within a mechanical system, all bushings and bearings shall be 
the same size, make and style, whenever possible. 
n. Sliding mechanism 
All sliding mechanisms shall have interchangeable replaceable wear points. 
o. Weldments 
All weldments shall be stress relieved. 
p. Heavy lift 
All large pieces of equipment shall have suitable lift holes or lugs. (i.e. power units for 
mezzanine) 
q. Purchasing parts 
The substitution of any manufacturer or product listed in the appendix shall require 
written approval of the METALSA engineering department 
r. Cushions 
Cushions shall be used at each end of the motion, either internal in the cylinder or 
externally via shock absorbers or both. 
s. Mechanical Motion 
Every mechanical motion shall be sensed at both ends of travel.

14.2.2 Rail System (Train Style) 
 
This system works as rollers gates system, the structure design and the wheel base 
adjustment are the same and this option will if the product design allows to adapt and 
hold the bracket of the rolling rail system. The main differences are: 
 
• 
The replacement of the roller beds with the rails. 
• 
The incorporation of the fourth mounting brackets on the ends of the product, the 
bearing (train wheel) to transfer frames and the physical lock. 
• 
The elimination of the third roller bed or support bar, the front and rear support bars 
and the containment barrier.

State of the art 27 values are affected when this happens. With the combination of both signals (RSSI 
and magnetometer values), the estimation of the person position is accomplished. By comparing the 
actual position with the previous position, movement commands are obtained and send to an 
Arduino. Afterwards, Arduino is in charge of sending the corresponding signals to the motors. One of 
the advantages of this work, is that no direct sight of line is required in order to find the person’s 
position. However, the results of the system were not accurate at calculating the true person’s 
position from the RSSI values37

28 Side Rails Box Section Fixtures 
 
28.1 Pre-Box Assembly Fixtures. (SNAP Fixture) 
 
This fixture concept applies only on low cycle time processes, and the main objective is to isolate the 
components loading time from the welding step in order to maximize the utilization of the weld 
equipment. (i.e. Lines with cycle time under 50sec) 
On this step the operator should apply some manual weld tacks to aviod the misalimeng of the parts 
during the transition the next fixture.

28.1.1 Box Weld Fixture 
 
• For box weld fixture there are two fixture concepts, that should be used based on 
the material specification. 
Strongback 
• This concept should used for assemblies with High Strength Steel 
compoentes.  
• Tooling bridge type design.Up/down clamp slide motion system with linear 
guides on both sides.  
• Lateral gap closing system, should use PHD (mongo) Brand equipment (model  
ML3106003).

All trunnion tables must be automatic, either with servomotor or with a rack and pinion mechanism. 
The subjection of the modules in this stations will consisto four clamping units at the corners of the 
mdule. Two options to use as clamping units: Power clamps or lock cylinders. Metalsa’s 
implementing team will define it during project revisión. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Beside the clamping units at this fixtures, pilots are needed when the assembly line has robotic 
transfer. There are two options for this: Pilots located at the trunnion table or Pilots located at the 
end effectors. 
NOTE: All tooling designs with manual trunnions are prohibited

36.3 Marriage table for main line 
modules 
At the main line marriage tables, the modules will be clamped in the first instance according to the 
GD & T, then auxiliaries will be added to help us control the modules to make the assembly. 
Scenarios: 
36.3.1 Our first scenario is when the GD&T asks you to control as follows: 
✓ “X” (F/A) y “Y” (C/C) On the crossmember IFS. 4-way fixed pilot 
✓ “Y” (C/C) on the spare tire crosspiece. 2-way fixed pilot 
✓ “Z” (U/D) in a diameter at the side rail web surface. Bull pin 2 roads 
 
In this case only frame clamps will be needed in the area where the marriage will take place, 
one that holds the front module, one that holds the rear module and the third one for the 
closure of the gap, 3 in total per side. 
Note: If more auxiliary units are required, they will be validated or revised during the 
design of the project.

welding process  is finished.

chassis only by adding an auxiliary unit (per side). If necessary, a second assistant (per side) will be 
discussed with the Metalsa implementation team during project reviews. Here is an example of this 
type of table:

36.7 Main line Trunnion inspection / repair tables 
 
All rotating inspection / rework tables must be automatic (with servo motor) and their clamping 
points will be only power clamps at the ends of the chassis to prevent it from falling at the time of 
inspection.

grease.

1. The vendor shall supply a machine data book for all equipment purchased, before 
the delivery date, and shall include, but not be limited to the following: 
a. Schematic of machine stations with descriptions of what happens at each station.  Use 
of a picture sheet or such is recommended. 
b. Estimated gross machine rates (by station and total machine). 
c. Discussion of features. 
d. Discussion of changeover or set-up, including approach and timing by station. 
e. List of assumptions or parameters the machine is based on. 
f. 
Operating instructions. 
g. Scaled floor plan showing the complete machine with electrical panels and all auxiliary 
equipment. 
 
Maintenance recommendations: 
h. Material requirements (oil specs.) 
i. 
Preventative maintenance frequencies 
j. 
Preventative maintenance procedures 
k. Tolerances 
l. 
Service or spare parts lists, including OEM part number (s), stocking recommendations 
and prices at time of machine data book delivery. 
m. Additional miscellaneous documentation or photographs to be included such as 
recommended foundations, certified foundation prints, pits, etc. 
n. Total power requirements of the machine in amperes, and at operating voltage. 
o. Water, compressed air and other utilities (natural gas, steam, exhaust, etc.) 
Requirements if any. 
p. The supplier must provide visuals for each operation in which is represented the location 
of the safety switches to disable the different types of energy (pneumatic, hydraulic, 
electrical, kinetic)

39 Appendix B  
 
39.1 Mechanical Documentation Required by Metalsa 
 
The following describes the required specifications for the documentation of mechanical 
drawings for the implementation of new projects or applications.  
For each project (new or refurbished) which requires manufacturing of a tooling of greater 
size than a mechanical unit, there must be two types of format regarding mechanical 
drawings that have to be turned in. These types are digital and printed format.  
Printed Format: 
Must elaborate a folder for each major assembly which will be divided in the structure 
shown below:  
 
Main Assemblies: For each main assembly must deliver two copies of folder in which it 
includes all its components that conform it in the way the diagram above describes it 
Units/Assemblies: Must be included the visual aids described in the previous diagram in 
each unit that makes up the assembly, followed by all the parts that conform it. 
Parts:  The parts’ headland must precede to the unit in which corresponds and also, it must 
be sectioned in the way the diagram describes it.  
Main
Assembly
•Mechanical Drawings with isometric and standard views (top, side, front) with reference 
measurements for general dimenssions.
•Mechanical Drawings for the detailing and specification of number of main units and 
subassemblies and its location (BOM)
•Drawings with MMC coordinates for the certification (in case required)
Main
Units 
•Mechanical Drawings with isometric and standard views (top, side, front) 
with reference measurements for general dimenssions.
•Mechanical drawings for identification of adjustment areas (shims) and 
the location points of the parts
•Mechanical drawings to reference list of materials and spare parts 
(BOM).
•BOM spreadsheet in which includes operation name, unit, supplier, 
brand, quantity, part number,description, comments.
Parts
•Detailed mechanical drawing for each piece specifying materials, 
tolerances and heat treatments.
•At the beginning of parts section should start with locating pins of the 
unit and wear parts

 
109 
 
 
Locating pin documents: 
Must deliver a separate document where the drawings of the pin locators and wear parts 
for each operation can be found for quick search. 
 
Digital Format: 
Must submit two sets of CDs or a pair of USB containing CMM report of the operation, 
3D models and the set of detailed drawings, both types of files MUST be in the following 
formats: 
3D Models: Must include STEP AP214 format, Solidworks format (in case of not be the 
native format the supplier will be responsible for translating files), also native file. 
 
2D Detailed drawings: Must be in DWG, PDF and Native format. 
 
Is required that each Main assembly includes a BOM file in excel containing listed all its 
spare parts with operation name to which it belongs, unit number, supplier, brand, 
quantity, part number, description and comments. 
Also should include a master file where the sum of all project operations is found.

40 Appendix C 
40.1 PLP Pin Design Requirements 
Locating Pins 
 All locating pins will be SAE 8620 steel or equivalent. Hardened to Rockwell C- 58-62 to a 
depth of .5 mm -2.0 mm- NAAMS (North American Automotive Metric Standard) pin locators 
are preferred. 
 
PLP Locating Pins for Geometry Stations & Weld Out Stations 
PLP locating pins for geometry stations shall be designed nominal to size of the gage hole 
minus 0.15mm + .00/-.02 as per NAAMS Global Standard Components- Assembly. PLP pins 
for weld out stations shall be designed nominal to size of gage hole minus 0.28mm + 0.00/-
0.02 as per NAAMS global standard Components- Assembly. 
 
PLP Locating Pins Extension Through Gage Holes  
PLP locating pins should extend through the gage holes a minimum length of 5mm and a 
maximum of 10mm, not including taper lead. 
 
 
 

 
116 
 
 
Datum Hole Design Requirements 
 
 
 
Note: 
The Preceding requirements are based on existing Chrysler Body in White Tool and Product 
Engineering Standards. They have been modified to suite the need of the chassis frame team

41 Appendix D 
 
41.1 Minimum thread engagements 
The length should be a least 1 1/2 times the outside diameter of the fastener 
Cast iron brass or bronze 
The length should be a least 2 times the outside diameter of the fastener 
Aluminum, plastic, and zinc 
The length should be a least 2 1/2 times the outside diameter of the fastener 
Socket head cap screws.  
 
 
Note:   torque to max. Spec. Only if parent material is of the same or higher quality than the 
bolt being used. 
After torquing is completed, draw a straight line (match mark) from the wall of the fastener 
head onto the seating surface using a white steel paint pen. Ensure that the line is easily visible 
for periodic inspection.

42 Appendix E 
All points of lubrication, monitoring, gauging, and filling shall be easily accessible and clearly 
identified.  Vendor shall supply drawings for all lubrication points, complete with schedule for 
preventive maintenance. 
 
Any grease nipple that can be damaged by moving parts shall be recessed.  A recess for a 
grease fitting shall be sized to accommodate a standard manual grease gun. 
No Copper Tubing 
 
Lubrication 
A) Lube fittings shall be manifold mounted and grouped to simplify servicing. 
B) Fittings shall be ¼” or 1/8” threaded zerk fittings.  Hammer type is not 
acceptable.  
C) Wherever practical, lube manifolds shall be located outside the equipment’s 
operating envelope and barrier guarding. 
D) Wherever practical, lube lines for moveable elements shall be routed to manifolds 
that have been secured to the moveable system to prevent line damage and 
fatigue. 
E) Manifolds shall be located 48” above floor or working platform.  Placement of 
manifolds at floor level is not acceptable. 
F) Lube lines shall be steel, copper and plastic lines are not acceptable. 
G) Line shall be properly secured. 
H) Compression fitting shall be three-piece nut and Ferrell. 
I) Equipment needing daily lubrication shall have an automatic centralized 
lubrication system, unless otherwise noted by Metalsa. 
J) Flow indicators shall be placed at every main distribution block. 
K) Critical components shall have a flow monitor at point of lubrication. 
L) Electrically operated components shall have a flow monitor. 
m) The main lubrication line shall have high pressure indicator pins installed.

44 Appendix  G 
44.1 Turning tables structure. 
a) The structure must be manufactured in only one piece. 
Even when the part design has different heights. According visual help. 
b) The bastidor structure in any moment must not have butt joints. 
c) The design must go through a finite element analysis to detect stress zones and 
correct, as they can cause any alteration in its structure and function. (Cracks, cracks in 
welding, and/or deformations.) 
d) With the gravity or mass center calculation, can be determine where and what 
dimensions the counterweights requires. 
e) The arrows diameter has to have a 30-40% protection in its capacity and must be hollow 
bar to move the table services (pneumatic, electric, sensor cables, etc.) 
f) The pillow block quantity depending of the arrows length, is 2 minimums to 4 per side. 
According the approved design by Metalsa engineering. 
g) Use max profile available ( As an Example 152.4 X 304.8 mm. Rectangular, with Con 12.7 
mm. Thickness or 254 mm x 12 .7 mm thickness.) 
h) By using a smaller caliber suffers major burn and changes in its structure that weakens, 
because we weld plates that have larger caliber as the tools bases, pin retainer, clamps 
etc. 
i) 
The table balancing must be on 0° with or without frame. 
j) 
The arrow holding the structure, shall be assembled considering male / female way. The 
weight should not be supported on fastening screws or weld supports. According visual 
help. 
k) Valves manifold should be at the ends of the table, not in the center for safety. 
l) 
The structure should have well supported bases, so that with the rotating system weight 
ht L structure don not bend.

53. Appendix O 
53.1. Lean Strongback 
To develop an interchangeable and lean concept for box side rails assemblies.  Provide cost effective 
solution to reduce the assembly initial investment and create capabilities to reuse the assets and 
space. 
 
53.1.1. Introduction and Purpose 
 
The following Supplier Standard is intended to provide guidelines for the development of the Lean 
Strongback Machine and to provide a quick, yet complete, overview of the system. 
The following technology aims to being an interchangeable and lean concept for box side rails 
assemblies by enabling reuse and enhancing assets life from one generation to another.  
 
Figure 2 Changeover Old Gen & New Gen 
 
53.2. Technical Guidelines 
Main Concepts – Lean Strongback 
 
53.2.1. Objective: 
Ensure that construction & testing of Lean Strongback guarantee repeatability, changeability, load 
capacity and ergonomics.  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 

 
134 
 
53.2.2. Assurance of piece location (fixtures) 
To ensure the side rail’s position and thus welding quality, locator pins or similar measures should be 
placed to ensure position repeatability and prevent piece movement induced by clamping: 
  
 
 
Figure 2.- Locator Pin ensures piece position and prevents 
piece movement. 
 
 
 
 
53.2.3. 
Robot reference position  
A reference should be placed to validate the correct position against to the docking station. 
 
 
  
                                          
Figure 3.- Robot reference fixture 
 
 
 
53.2.4.  Lean Design 
 
Lean Design relies on the definition and optimization of values coupled with the prevention of 
wastes before they enter the system. Because of this value definition, Lean Design was defined to 
accomplish machine size and cost reduction and to increase machine flexibility and efficiency (cost-
benefit-time). 
Compact high thrust actuators should be selected. Mechanisms and fixtures should be designed to 
fully take advantage of the actuators’ qualities; resulting in footprint and tooling components 
reduction.  
 
 
 
 
 

 
135 
 
 
Figure 4..- Current Strongback (left) VS Lean Strongback. New design reduced footpint and tooling components size 
and number drastically. 
53.2.5. Actuator Dimensioning 
Previous piece analysis has to be made to ensure the adequate actuator selection. Oversizing and 
undersizing pneumatic actuator is a practice that doesn’t comply with the Lean Design concept. The 
following parameters need to be evaluated before selecting any actuator: 
1) Piece geometry 
2) Piece’s needed input force to ensure positioning and prevent torsion 
3) Actuator max force output 
4) Piece’s real conditions / previous process 
Also it is important that every actuator with a vertical motion (pushing or position) or clamping 
motion must include means to ensure position isn’t compromised by air supply cut off, both for 
safety and quality reasons. This means can include but aren’t limited to: 
• 
Pneumatic brakes 
• 
Mechanical brakes 
• 
Physical barriers 
 
53.2.6. Squeezing Fingers Positioning 
Some considerations have to be made to ensure the maximum possible clamping force is obtained 
from the frame clamps: 
1) The distance between the pushing fingers’ furthest pressing point from the welding line has 
to be 5 mm.  If exceeded, finger integrity and clamping force are compromised. 
 
 
Figure 5.- “d” Distance must be at least 5 mm. 
 
 
 
 

 
136 
 
 
2) Distance between squeezing fingers and frame clamp pivot: The distance between the pivot and 
the clamped piece should be kept as short as possible as clamping force decreases if this 
distance increases.  
To further illustrate this point, we present the following example doing the clamping force 
calculation for one of the pushing fingers on frame clamp U05: 
Machine current conditions: 
• 
Working air pressure [P]:7 bar 
• 
Distance from Pivot to piece [d]:252.68 mm 
• 
*Clamp force multiplier [Cf]: 595440 
 
 
Figure 6.- Frame clamp U05 with four pushing fingers 
 
𝑇𝑜𝑡𝑎𝑙 𝑐𝑙𝑎𝑚𝑝 𝑓𝑜𝑟𝑐𝑒: 𝐶𝑓∗𝑃
𝑑
= 595440 ∗7
252.68
= 16,495 [𝑁] 
 
3) Distance between jaws: To ensure max clamping force is achieved the jaws have to reach 
their final closing position within the high force region. The high force region. For reference 
the high force region starts 3 mm before the jaw closing position (when the two jaws are 
parallel): 
 
Figure 47.- High Force Region 
 

 
137 
 
 
4) Working Pressure: At least 0.5 MPa pressure has to be supplied to achieve maximum 
clamping force. 
5) A simulation needs to be run on the piece to be clamped in order to determine the needed 
clamping force according to the pieces’ geometry. An example of an arrangement is shown. 
6) Squeezing fingers per Frame Clamp: The squeezing fingers per frame clamp are to be 
defined according to the piece-to-be-clamped challenges. The current side rails present 
different heights, widths and thicknesses all along the piece, thus a finger arrangement was 
proposed and a similar exercise should be made for every new application. Necessary input 
simulations should also be made to ensure allowable piece gap is obtained.  
 
Figure 7.- Box side rails proposed division

53.2.7. Finger slot adjustment 
Shims can be used to make adjustments in finger positioning, however, permissible jaw distance 
must be taken into account to ensure clamping force output is not compromised.  
 
Figure 9.- Shims can be placed both for height and depth purposes. 
 
Because shims can be placed both for finger height and finger depth purposes, the following 
limitations have to be taken into account: 
• 
Finger height should always be 5 mm form welding line. (see Distance Between Fingers and 
Welding Line. 
• 
Finger depth should not compromise jaw closing distance 
 
53.2.8. Bridge Dimensioning 
The bridge’s main function is to ensure the piece’s positioning and avoid torsion during the welding 
process. A fatigue, reactive force and torsion analysis has to be made to ensure the bridge’s 
durability.  
 
Figure 10..- Current Strongback Bridge fatigue life simulation using SIMUFACT 
 
 
 
 

 
139 
 
53.2.9. Ergonomics 
 
Lean Strongback is intended to be re used in more than 65% once Tacoma production ends. That is 
why ergonomics becomes an important subject. The machine’s current height doesn’t comply with 
ergonomic guidelines. Optimal machine height should be between 35 and 43 inches. 
 
 
 
Figure 11.- Piece deposit height should 
be between 34 and 48 inches 
 
 
 
 
53.2.10. 
Welding process optimization 
A tack weld pre process should be implemented before the arc welding takes place to prevent piece 
distortion induced by welding heat. This step could not only help for quality purposes but actually 
help to eliminate the tack weld process that is currently done in a separate process. 
Tack weld pre process is restricted to cycle time. If cycle time allows it, tack weld system pre process 
should be implemented.  
 
 
Figure 12.- Tack welding pre process was introduced to avoid piece distortion. 
 
 
 
 

 
140 
 
53.3. Main Concepts -  Cart Tooling 
 
53.3.1. Objective: 
Guarantee that Construction & Testing of Cart Tooling complies with repeatability, changeability, 
load capacity and ergonomics.  
 
53.3.2. Assurance of docking location (repeatability) 
Plungers embedded with a position sensor should be placed to ensure the tooling position with 
reference to the docking station. 
    
53.3.3. Tooling Mobility  
Free axis wheels should be placed on every tooling corner to achieve full mobility. To support the 
tooling’s whole weight, bearings should be placed on every corner as well. Weight is distributed 
between the wheels and bearings; the bearings must be sized to withstand the structure weight in 
case of dirt accumulation on the wheels.  
 
 
 
Figure 13.- Bearings are placed alongside wheels to support the 
structure weight and enable free axis mobility. 
 
 
 
 
 
53.3.4. Docking Station  
 
Fixed steering makes maneuvering easy. A 5th wheel hitch configuration must be considered to allow 
more maneuverability and enable swinging or locking in place.  
Figure 14.- Docking station and Cart Tool 
 
 
 

 
141 
 
It is extremely important to consider the docking station as a base for future platforms (next gen) since 
it will be where the next tool will be received, that is, maintaining the relation of the elements with 
respect to the docking station will be critical to be able to have a good management and to take 
advantage of system reuse. 
 
 
Figure 15.-  Docking Station 
53.3.5. Cart Tool 
This element is part of the reconfigurable system and one cart tooling per fixture should be 
considered. Because of this, it will be dedicated to a tool and will be considered as a tooling amount. 
It is important to consider the measurements of the docking (base) to match the dimensions and 
characteristics of the cart tooling shown below: 
 
Figure 16.-  Cart Tooling 
 
Consider a height offset of 2.7 mm from the wheel to the base of the docking station to rule out the 
height of the wheels, in case of accumulation of dirt on the wheels, the dependence of the axle " z” 
will be transferred to the bearings that have contact with the tracks: 
 
Figure 17..- Wheels and bearings  carry Lean Sreongack’s whol weight. 

 
142 
 
 
The cart must be limited to 25,000 pounds (11,340 kg). 
 
 
Figure 18.- Tooling handling is made possible by the combination of the docking station concept and the cart tool. 
 
 
53.4.  Repeatability studies 
 
The following studies must be made at tool liberation to ensure the machine is reliable. 
• 
R&R - Static (Docking & Fixture)  
• 
R&R - Dynamic (Docking & Fixture)  
• 
R&R – Dynamic (Material & Fixture)  
 
 
53.5. Simulations and Analysis 
 
Although the concept is flexible and can be subject to changes the following simulations must be run 
with every proposal to ensure viability and feasibility. See design guidelines for an example: 
• 
Welding process simulation 
• 
Piece distortion both clamped (hot) and unclamped (cold) 
• 
Bridge reactive force analysis 
• 
Bridge fatigue life prediction 
• 
Process cycle time simulation

1 Purpose 
The purpose of this standard is to ensure the safety of Metalsa's ENNs and their respective 
equipment, as well as that of their assets through guidelines and considerations to be 
considered in the design phase of the structure. 
 
As well as the registration of best practices that aim to maintain the operational safety of 
those involved in the mezzanine. 
 
2 Introduction 
These guidelines are the standard that all Metalsa Assembly projects must follow to 
maximize the use of the required footprint and ensure the operator safety and Metalsa lines 
equipment. 
 
3 Objective 
The objective of this standard is to provide guidance to process engineers, Value 
Proposition, and external suppliers to ensure the proper design of a structure such as the 
Mezzanine. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 

 
 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
4 Mezzanine 
Mezzanines allow to multiply the useful area of any space by enabling storage areas both 
on the ground level and on the upper levels. 
 
The structure is composed of columns, beams and a floor, the floor can be implemented 
in materials such as steel grating, fiber cement and wood.  Mezzanines are versatile 
structures of great adaptability covering almost any load situation and floor plan 
distribution.  
 
 
4.1 When is recommended to use Mezzanine? 
The use of the mezzanine is recommended only if there are floor space restrictions, so 
in this case you could move the peripheral equipment to the mezzanine. 
 
Example of Mezzanine extracted from BT1 line layout 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 

 
 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent.

NOTE: Ensure that the fume extraction system performs its function properly to prevent 
welding fumes to reach the controller fans above the mezzanine and cause 
damage/wear. 
 
PDPs are not allowed to be incorporated into the mezzanine as they are equipment that 
requires relatively "common" use and must be kept on the floor. In order for the MCP to 
be mounted above the mezzanine, it must be ensured that there is a connection port at 
floor level to avoid having people constantly on top of it. In addition, to determine the 
weight, it is first necessary to determine the number of stations and equipment to be 
powered. 
 
The 12" cable tray is ideal for a single station (2 robots and 2 welding machines), there 
can be different arrangements of how to use the cable tray and the width to be used, 
and this will depend on each project. 
 
6 Regulations to be fulfilled for its construction 
It must be ensured that the mezzanine can support its own weight (dead weight), plus 
that of the number of items listed in the table above, the approximate weight of the 
number of people that can be on top at the same time as determined by the 
maintenance and EH&S team. Plus, an extra safety capacity determined by the 
structure's safety certifying house and Metalsa's EH&S team. 
 
The construction/design of the mezzanine must comply with OSHA guidelines and 
those applicable to each region, in addition to being certified by a safety certification 
company applicable to each region of the country where the construction of the 
mezzanine is going to be built. 

 
 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
The design of the mezzanine, stairways, and ladders (if any) and many of the best 
safe practices must comply with the requirements presented in this standard, 
with the Occupational Safety and Health Administration (OSHA) standards and 
those applicable to each region. It is IMPORTANT and MANDATORY to read the 
applicable OSHA standards for mezzanine design and follow best safety practices 
in addition to those included in this standard. 
 
7 Safe practices for mezzanine design 
 
7.1 Fall protection systems and falling object protection (Handrails 
guardrails and others) 
The use of spiral staircases or designs that are too steep is prohibited. If a ladder or 
other vertical access is included in the design, it must be validated by the EH&S team 
and comply with OSHA and regional fall protection requirements. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Beams near to the material access door and those that are close to the aisle where the 
tuggers or forklifts circulate must have beam protection. All mezzanine columns (the 
entire structure) are intended to support forklift or tugger impacts.

Duty to have fall protection and falling object protection.

Fall protection systems and falling object protection-criteria and practices. 
(Standard Number: 1910.29) 
 
Among the main points, but not the only ones, we find that the following must be 
complied with: 
 
7.2 Guardrails 
 
The guardrails must be painted in Yellow 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(1) 
The top edge height of top rails, or equivalent guardrail system members, are 42 inches (107 
cm), plus or minus 3 inches (8 cm), above the walking-working surface. The top edge height may 
exceed 45 inches (114 cm), provided the guardrail system meets all other criteria of paragraph 
(b) of this section (see Figure D–11 of this section). 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(2) 
Midrails, screens, mesh, intermediate vertical members, solid panels, or equivalent intermediate 
members are installed between the walking-working surface and the top edge of the guardrail 
system as follows when there is not a wall or parapet that is at least 21 inches (53 cm) high: 
 
 
 

 
 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(2)(i) 
Midrails are installed at a height midway between the top edge of the guardrail system and the 
walking-working surface. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(2)(ii) 
Screens and mesh extend from the walking-working surface to the top rail and along the entire 
opening between top rails supports. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(2)(iii) 
Intermediate vertical members (such as balusters) are installed no more than 19 inches (48 cm) 
apart; and 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(2)(iv) 
Other equivalent intermediate members (such as additional midrails and architectural panels) are 
installed so that the openings are not more than 19 inches (48 cm) wide. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(3) 
Guardrail systems are capable of withstanding, without failure, a force of at least 200 pounds 
(890 N) applied in a downward or outward direction within 2 inches (5 cm) of the top edge, at any 
point along the top rail. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(4) 
When the 200-pound (890-N) test load is applied in a downward direction, the top rail of the 
guardrail system must not deflect to a height of less than 39 inches (99 cm) above the walking-
working surface. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(5) 
Midrails, screens, mesh, intermediate vertical members, solid panels, and other equivalent 
intermediate members are capable of withstanding, without failure, a force of at least 150 
pounds (667 N) applied in any downward or outward direction at any point along the 
intermediate member. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(6) 
Guardrail systems are smooth-surfaced to protect employees from injury, such as punctures or 
lacerations, and to prevent catching or snagging of clothing. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(7) 
The ends of top rails and midrails do not overhang the terminal posts, except where the 
overhang does not pose a projection hazard for employees. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(8) 
Steel banding and plastic banding are not used for top rails or midrails. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(9) 
Top rails and midrails are at least 0.25-inches (0.6 cm) in diameter or in thickness. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(10) 
When guardrail systems are used at hoist areas, a removable guardrail section, consisting of a 
top rail and midrail, are placed across the access opening between guardrail sections when 
employees are not performing hoisting operations. The employer may use chains or gates 
instead of a removable guardrail section at hoist areas if the employer demonstrates the chains 
or gates provide a level of safety equivalent to guardrails. 

 
 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
7.3 Handrails 
The Handrails must be painted in Yellow 
 
• 
1910.29(f)(1)(i) 
Handrails are not less than 30 inches (76 cm) and not more than 38 inches (97 cm), as 
measured from the leading edge of the stair tread to the top surface of the handrail (see Figure 
D-12 of this section). 
 
 
• 
1910.29(f)(1)(ii)(B) 
The height of stair rail systems installed is not less than 42 inches (107 cm) from the leading 
edge of the stair tread to the top surface of the top rail. 
 
• 
1910.29(f)(1)(iii) 
The top rail of a stair rail system may serve as a handrail only when: 
 
• 
1910.29(f)(1)(iii)(A) 
The height of the stair rail system is not less than 36 inches (91 cm) and not more than 38 inches 
(97 cm) as measured at the leading edge of the stair tread to the top surface of the top rail (see 
Figure D-13 of this section) 
 
 
• 
1910.29(f)(1)(iii)(B) 
The top rail of the stair rail system meets the other handrail requirements in paragraph (f) of this 
section. 
 
• 
1910.29(f)(2) 
The minimum clearance between handrails and any other object is 2.25 inches (5.7 cm). 
 
 

 
 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
• 
1910.29(f)(3) 
Handrails and stair rail systems are smooth-surfaced to protect employees from injury, such as 
punctures or lacerations, and to prevent catching or snagging of clothing. 
 
• 
1910.29(f)(4) 
No opening in a stair rail system exceeds 19 inches (48 cm) at its least dimension. 
 
• 
1910.29(f)(5) 
Handrails have the shape and dimension necessary so that employees can grasp the handrail 
firmly. 
 
• 
1910.29(f)(7) 
Handrails and the top rails of stair rail systems are capable of withstanding, without failure, a 
force of at least 200 pounds (890 N) applied in any downward or outward direction within 2 
inches (5 cm) of any point along the top edge of the rail. 
 
7.4 Covers 
• 
1910.29(e) 
The employer must ensure each cover for a hole in a walking-working surface: 
 
• 
1910.29(e)(1) 
Is capable of supporting without failure, at least twice the maximum intended load that may be 
imposed on the cover at any one time. 
 
• 
1910.29(e)(2) 
Is secured to prevent accidental displacement. 
 
• Avoid Irving mesh and consider as best practice an anti-skid sheet. A carbon steel 
sheet with a diamond or five-bar relief would be best. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
• The mezzanine should have a yellow (same as the handrails) barrier at the edge of 
the platform (skirting/Toe board) to prevent things from falling from above.

anti-skid reliefs

7.5 Protection from falling objects (Skirting/Toe board) 
The skirting/toe board must be painted in yellow 
 
• 
1910.29(k)(1) 
The employers must ensure toe boards used for falling object protection: 
 
• 
1910.29(k)(1)(i) 
Are erected along the exposed edge of the overhead walking-working surface for a length that is 
sufficient to protect employees below. 
 
• 
1910.29(k)(1)(ii) 
Have a minimum vertical height of 3.5 inches (9 cm) as measured from the top edge of the toe 
board to the level of the walking-working surface. 
 
• 
1910.29(k)(1)(iii) 
Do not have more than a 0.25-inch (0.5-cm) clearance or opening above the walking-working 
surface. 
 
• 
1910.29(k)(1)(iv) 
Are solid or do not have any opening that exceeds 1 inch (3 cm) at its greatest dimension. 
 
• 
1910.29(k)(1)(v) 
Have a minimum height of 2.5 inches (6 cm) when used around vehicle repair, service, or 
assembly pits.  
 
• 
1910.29(k)(1)(vi) 
Are capable of withstanding, without failure, a force of at least 50 pounds (222 N) applied in any 
downward or outward direction at any point along the toe board.

7.6 Stairways 
To know all the guidelines that Metalsa requires for the design and construction of 
stairways, please visit the following link to the OSHA standard: 
 
Click here to consult the OSHA Standard about: Stairways  
(Standard Number: 1910.25) 
 
Among the main points, but not the only ones, we find that the following must be 
complied with: 
 
• 1910.25(b)(1) 
Handrails, stair railing systems, and guardrail systems are provided in accordance with Sec. 
1910.28. 
 
• 
1910.25(b)(2) 
The vertical clearance above any stair tread to any overhead obstruction is at least 6 feet 8 
inches (203 cm), measured from the front edge of the tread. Spiral stairways must comply with 
the vertical clearance requirements in paragraph (d)(3) of this section. 
 
• 
1910.25(b)(4) 
Stairway landings and platforms are at least the width of the stairway and at least 30 inches (76 
cm) deep, measured in the direction of travel. 
 
• 
1910.25(b)(5)(ii) 
Less than 22 inches (56 cm) for platforms installed on or after January 17, 2017  
 
 
 
• 
1910.25(b)(6) 
Each ladder may support at least five times the normal anticipated live load, but never less than 
a concentrated load of 1000 pounds (454 kg) applied at any point. 
 
• 
1910.25(b)(7) 
Standard ladders are used to provide access from one walking and working surface to another 
when operations require regular and routine travel between levels, including access to operating 
platforms for equipment. Spiral stairways may be used on tanks and similar round structures 
when the diameter of the tank or structure is at least 5 feet (1.5 m). 
 
 
 

 
 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
 
• 
1910.25(c)(1) 
Installed at angles of 30 to 50 degrees to the 
horizontal. 
 
• 
1910.25(c)(2) 
Have a maximum riser height of 9.5 inches (24 
cm). 
 
• 
1910.25(c)(3) 
Have a minimum tread depth of 9.5 inches (24 
cm) 
 
• 
1910.25(c)(4) 
Have a minimum width of 22 inches (56 cm) 
between vertical barriers  
 
 
 
 
In addition to the requirements provided by the OSHA standard, Metalsa asks that the 
following requirements be met: 
 
• The position and design of this staircases will be linked 
to the conditions/spaces of the floor layout, although it 
has to be oriented to the nearest emergency exits to 
facilitate the evacuation of people in case of 
emergency.  
 
 
• The design of the stairs to the mezzanine should have an intermediate landing and a 
"closed" design that prevents liquid as well as solid materials from falling from above.

7.7 Fixed Ladders 
To know all the guidelines that Metalsa requires for the design and construction and 
design of ladders in if is accepted by the EH&S team and maintenance, please visit the 
following link to the OSHA standard: 
 
Click here to consult the OSHA Standard about: Ladders  
(Standard Number: 1910.23)  
 
Among the main points, but not the only ones, we find that the following must be 
complied with: 
 
• 
1910.23(b)(1) 
Ladder rungs, steps, and cleats are parallel, level, and uniformly spaced when the ladder is in 
position for use. 
 
• 
1910.23(b)(2) 
Ladder rungs, steps, and cleats are spaced not less than 10 inches (25 cm) and not more than 
14 inches (36 cm) apart, as measured between the centerlines of the rungs, cleats, and steps 
 
• 
1910.23(b)(6) 
Metal ladders are made with corrosion-resistant material or protected against corrosion. 
 
• 
1910.23(b)(7) 
Ladder surfaces are free of puncture and laceration hazards. 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(1) 
Fixed ladders are capable of supporting their maximum intended load. 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(2) 
The minimum perpendicular distance from the centerline of the steps or rungs, or grab bars, or 
both, to the nearest permanent object in back of the ladder is 7 inches (18 cm), except for 
elevator pit ladders, which have a minimum perpendicular distance of 4.5 inches (11 cm). 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(3) 
Grab bars do not protrude on the climbing side beyond the rungs of the ladder that they serve. 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(4) 
The side rails of through or side-step ladders extend at least 42 inches (1.1 m) above the top of 
the access level or landing platform served by the ladder. For parapet ladders, the access level 
is: 
• 
1910.23(d)(4)(i) 
The roof if the parapet is cut to permit passage through the parapet; or 
 
 
 
 

 
 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(4)(ii) 
The top of the parapet if the parapet is continuous. 
• 
1910.23(d)(5) 
For through ladders, the steps or rungs are omitted from the extensions, and the side rails are 
flared to provide not less than 24 inches (61cm) and not more than 30 inches (76 cm) of 
clearance. When a ladder safety system is provided, the maximum clearance between side rails 
of the extension must not exceed 36 inches (91 cm). 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(6) 
For side-step ladders, the side rails, rungs, and steps must be continuous in the extension (see 
Figure D-2 of this section). 
 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(7) 
Grab bars extend 42 inches (1.1 m) above the access level or landing platforms served by the 
ladder. 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(8) 
The minimum size (cross-section) of grab bars is the same size as the rungs of the ladder. 
 
 
 
 

 
 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(9) 
When a fixed ladder terminates at a hatch (see Figure D-3 of this section), the hatch cover: 
 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(9)(i) 
Opens with sufficient clearance to provide easy access to or from the ladder. 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(9)(ii) 
Opens at least 70 degrees from horizontal if the hatch is counterbalanced. 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(10) 
Individual-rung ladders are constructed to prevent the employee's feet from sliding off the ends 
of the rungs (see Figure D-4 of this section). 
 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(11) 
Fixed ladders having a pitch greater than 90 degrees from the horizontal are not used. 
 
 

 
 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(12) 
The step-across distance from the centerline of the rungs or steps is: 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(12)(i) 
For through ladders, not less than 7 inches (18 cm) and not more than 12 inches (30 cm) to the 
nearest edge of the structure, building, or equipment accessed from the ladders. 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(12)(ii) 
For side-step ladders, not less than 15 inches (38 cm) and not more than 20 inches (51 cm) to 
the access points of the platform edge. 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(13) 
Fixed ladders that do not have cages or wells have: 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(13)(i) 
A clear width of at least 15 inches (38 cm) on each side of the ladder centerline to the nearest 
permanent object; and 
 
• 
1910.23(d)(13)(ii) 
A minimum perpendicular distance of 30 inches (76 cm) from the centerline of the steps or rungs 
to the nearest object on the climbing side. When unavoidable obstructions are encountered, the 
minimum clearance at the obstruction may be reduced to 24 inches (61 cm), provided deflector 
plates are installed (see Figure D-5 of this section). 
NOTE: 
Section 1910.28 establishes the employer's duty to provide fall protection for employees on fixed 
ladders, and § 1910.29 specifies the criteria for fall protection systems for fixed ladders. 
 
 
NOTE: Since cages are not considered as a protection fall system by OSHA it's 
mandatory to use a retrieval system to use ladders (review: “ladders best practices 
to use” to know more about the fall protection systems)

Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
7.8 Material Access Gate 
 
The purpose of this gate is to serve as an access to upload the previously mentioned 
devices (welding machines, controllers, etc.).  
 
It is recommended that the enabling of this access be left to the consideration of the 
maintenance team and EH&S as "ideally" it should not be used on a regular basis, so 
there would be no need to enable this access as all items can be climbed prior to 
placing the handrail at the mezzanine construction stage.  
 
The width of the material access door must be at least 700 mm (according to the widest 
controller R-30iA). 
To know all the guidelines that Metalsa requires for the design and construction of the 
material access gate if is accepted by the EH&S and Maintenance team, please visit the 
following link to the OSHA standard: 
 
Click here to consult the OSHA Standard about:  
Fall protection systems and falling object protection-criteria and practices. 
(Standard Number: 1910.29) 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(10) 
When guardrail systems are used at hoist areas, a removable guardrail section, consisting of a 
top rail and midrail, are placed across the access opening between guardrail sections when 
employees are not performing hoisting operations. The employer may use chains or gates 
instead of a removable guardrail section at hoist areas if the employer demonstrates the chains 
or gates provide a level of safety equivalent to guardrails. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(11) 
When guardrail systems are used around holes, they are installed on all unprotected sides or 
edges of the hole. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(12) 
For guardrail systems used around holes through which materials may be passed: 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(12)(i) 
When materials are being passed through the hole, not more than two sides of the guardrail 
system are removed: and 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(12)(ii) 
When materials are not being passed through the hole, the hole must be guarded by a guardrail 
system along all unprotected sides or edges or closed over with a cover. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(13) 
When guardrail systems are used around holes that serve as points of access (such as 
ladderways), the guardrail system opening: 
 
 

 
 
 
Copyright © Metalsa, S.A. de C.V. Carretera Miguel Alemán Km. 16.5 No. 100, Apodaca Nuevo León, México, 66600. 2017 
Complete or partial reproduction of this material is prohibited without the owner’s explicit consent. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(13)(i) 
Has a self-closing gate that slides or swings away from the hole and is equipped with a top rail 
and midrail or equivalent intermediate member that meets the requirements in paragraph (b) of 
this section; or is offset to prevent an employee from walking or falling into the hole. 
 
• 
1910.29(b)(14) 
Guardrail systems on ramps and runways are installed along each unprotected side or edge. 
 
7.8.1 Anchor point 
To know all the guidelines that Metalsa requires for the design and construction of the 
anchor point, please visit the following link to the OSHA standard: 
 
Click here to consult the OSHA Standard about:  
Personal fall protection systems. 
(Standard Number: 1910.140) 
 
The anchor point can be in the mezzanine, anchored to a PTR 2 meters from the edge 
of the material access door or similarly to an elevated point outside the mezzanine, this 
will be defined by the mezzanine integrator in conjunction with the EH&S team. This 
point should support up to 5000 pounds (similar to the force caused by an operator's 
free fall). 
 
The harness to be used by the operator must be similar to the "self-retracting" harness 
shown in the photo and must be suitable for working at heights, as this type of harness 
detects a sudden change in harness speed and therefore stops or slows down the 
operator's movement. This ensures that the operator does not suffer a fall.

7.8.2 Conditions to use forklifts or hoists 
The void generated under the material access door between the two mezzanine columns 
must be covered by a fence to protect/prevent any component from falling from the 
forklift from hitting any equipment, people, or material under the mezzanine. And it also 
depends on the frequency with which the forklift is used to lower or raise things, if it is too 
often, it is necessary to use this mesh, (more than 1-2 times by month) otherwise it is not 
necessary. 
 
 
The space conditions in the layout for a forklift to maneuver is a minimum of 3.5 m or 
11.5 ft. This ensures that there is enough room to maneuver with safe clearances. If a 
hoist is used, a minimum clearance of 2.5 m or 8.2 ft. is required, in addition to 
having an area limitation on the floor determined by the reach of the hoist indicating that 
this area is for suspended loads.

It must also be ensured that the pedestrian walkway is not next to the material access 
door. The protocol to follow to limit traffic in the area when material is being brought up 
to the mezzanine is to use any indication or material that limits traffic to the area, 
whether it is yellow tape, cones, or posts, leaving the EH&S team to decide what is 
most convenient for them.

8.1.1 Material and Access to the mezzanine gates 
• These doors must be locked with padlocks, the keys, or combinations of which must 
be in the possession of authorized maintenance personnel. 
 
• The door that allows access to materials and equipment must have a Safety Sign 
that specifies that in order to open the door, the operator must be wearing all PPE 
along with the harness anchored to the anchor point and must have the proper 
authorization to open the door and proceed with the corresponding activities.

8.1.2 Ladders best practices use 
• 
1910.23(b)(9) 
Ladders are inspected prior to initial use on each work shift, and more frequently as needed, to 
identify any visible defects that could cause injury to employees. 
 
• 
1910.23(b)(10) 
Any ladder with structural or other defects is immediately labeled "Dangerous: do not use" or 
similar language in accordance with § 1910.145 and removed from service until repaired in 
accordance with 1910.22(d) or replaced. 
 
• 
1910.23(b)(11) 
Each employee faces the ladder when ascending or descending the ladder. 
 
• 
1910.23(b)(12) 
Each employee uses at least one hand to grasp the ladder when ascending and descending. 
 
 
• 
1910.23(b)(13) 
No employee carries any object or load that may cause the employee to lose balance and fall 
while ascending or descending the ladder. 
 
 
Ladder safety systems.  
 
• 
1910.29(i)(1) 
Each ladder safety system allows the employee to climb up and down using both hands and 
does not require that the employee continuously hold, push, or pull any part of the system while 
climbing. 
 
• 
1910.29(i)(2) 
The connection between the carrier or lifeline and the point of attachment to the body harness or 
belt does not exceed 9 inches (23 cm). 
 
• 
1910.29(i)(3) 
Mountings for rigid carriers are attached at each end of the carrier, with intermediate mountings 
spaced, as necessary, along the entire length of the carrier so the system has the strength to 
stop employee falls. 
 
• 
1910.29(i)(4) 
Mountings for flexible carriers are attached at each end of the carrier and cable guides for 
flexible carriers are installed at least 25 feet (7.6 m) apart but not more than 40 feet (12.2 m) 
apart along the entire length of the carrier. 
 
• 
1910.29(i)(5) 
The design and installation of mountings and cable guides does not reduce the design strength 
of the ladder. 
 
• 
1910.29(i)(6) 
Ladder safety systems and their support systems are capable of withstanding, without failure, a 
drop test consisting of an 18-inch (41-cm) drop of a 500-pound (227-kg) weight.
